Assassin of French President

Russian Criminal Executed on the Guillotine

Escorted to the Execution Ground in the Early Morning Dawn

Remembers His Motherland Before Execution

Paris Dispatch from the National Press, 14th: The Russian criminal Goguloff, the assassin of former French President Doumer, was executed on the guillotine outside the Santey Prison in Paris this morning. At approximately 6:03 a.m., the blade fell, and the head and body fell into separate baskets. The execution was completed in five minutes, and the body was taken away by horse-drawn carriage and buried in the Ivry Cemetery. Thousands of people watched the execution, but due to the strict security and the speed of the execution, few were able to witness the execution.

Paris Dispatch from Havas, 14th: Goguloff, the assassin of the former French President, was executed at 5:52 a.m. this morning. The crowd was unprecedentedly large. Since last night, the crowd had gathered, and barriers were set up 40 meters from the execution ground to prevent the crowd from rushing in, so about 1,500 spectators were blocked from seeing the execution. Last night at 2:00 a.m., the execution stake was erected, and the executioner and his assistants, all dressed in white cloth shirts and trousers, made their final preparations. A scaffold was set up a few meters away, appearing as a black shadow in the clear night. The execution stake was set up in front of the prison wall between two elm trees, behind which was a white wooden fence. During the night, Goguloff slept peacefully in his narrow bed in the prison, like an ordinary person. Another prisoner shared the same room with him. The lights in the room remained on all night, and the guards constantly peered through the gaps in the door to observe the prisoner's sleeping state. At 4:30 a.m., Dr. Paul, a forensic doctor, arrived at the prison. Soon after, the Prosecutor General of the French Republic and the prisoner's defense lawyers, Rérolle and Roger, also arrived. Before entering the prison cell, Rérolle told reporters that Goguloff's wife intended to retrieve her husband's body. Soon after, the executioner reported to the judge that the execution procedures were ready. Then, they urged the criminal to wake up. When the judge entered the room, the prisoner was still sound asleep. When the judge called him to wake up, the prisoner heard the noise from outside, but showed no sign of panic. After a moment, he seemed to realize something and mumbled a few words. Then, the prisoner changed into a wide-necked shirt, and the executioners cut off some of the long hair hanging down from his neck. At this time, the guards at the execution ground all drew their swords. The street lights were extinguished, and the executioners surrounding the scaffold, along with their two main assistants, were now dressed in black and wore skullcaps. The prisoner was given a religious salvation ceremony by a priest and quietly listened to Mass, followed by baptism. Then, he uttered a few words, saying, "I am neither a royalist nor a communist. I die for my cause, just like all the peasants in Russia who are oppressed by the Reds." The prisoner drank two glasses of red wine, but refused the cigarettes offered. Afterwards, the prisoner entered the execution ground with the priest and his defense lawyers. At this time, he said to those around him, "Please tell my wife that I love her very much. I have caused my wife to suffer. I beg her to forgive me, and I hope that my wife can raise our soon-to-be-born child to adulthood and that he will continue to believe in my cause in the future. Now, I am dying for this good cause." After speaking, Goguloff revealed his strong chest in front of the scaffold, with no expression on his face. The two executioner's assistants helped him down, as Goguloff's legs were tied and he could not climb down the ladder. When approaching the scaffold, Goguloff's attitude was different from that of ordinary criminals. He only stared at the execution machine, without showing any fear. At that time, Goguloff spoke softly to himself, but it could be heard clearly, saying, "Please forgive me." The priest covered the prisoner's head with the sleeve of his black robe, so as not to distress him by seeing the guillotine. The priest then embraced the prisoner, and Rérolle kissed the prisoner goodbye. After the executioners had set up the execution machine, the prisoner was still heard muttering to himself, saying, "Oh, France, my motherland." Then, with a sudden sound, the blade fell, and the execution was extremely quick, very different from usual. It took less than ten seconds from start to finish. By 6:05 a.m., the execution ground on the Avenue d'Arago had been cleaned, the scaffold had been dismantled, and the barriers on the road had been removed. The spectators who had waited for a long time, having seen nothing, returned disappointed. In a short time, the execution site was covered with fresh sand, leaving no trace to be found.

Match King

Engaged in Scams Before His Death

Liquidator Releases Preliminary Report

Stockholm Dispatch from Reuters, 13th: The preliminary report of the liquidator of the estate of Match King Kreuger was published in the newspapers today, referring to Kreuger as a criminal, not a businessman. The report analyzes the large-scale scams set up by Kreuger, saying that Kreuger thought of himself as a great man, but he was not. Kreuger, after failing to maintain his nominal business, engaged in fabricating rumors of huge profits in order to maintain the impression of his financial stability. What distinguished him from ordinary people was that he was a criminal. The directors of Kreuger & Toll knew that Kreuger's various reports and documents regarding the company's position were false.

News

Zhao Pi-lian Passes Through Jinan on His Way to Beijing 5

Jinan Correspondence: Central Committee member Zhao Pi-lian passed through Jinan at 9:30 this morning (the 13th) on the Pǔpǔ Line Train No. 201, representing Yan Xishan, the Pacification Commissioner of Taiyuan, to make contact with the Central Government. I interviewed him on the train, asking about his mission in Beijing. Zhao said, "I don't have any particular mission on this trip to Beijing. However, in this time of national crisis, those who bear the responsibility of the Central Government must gather in Nanjing and work together to overcome the national crisis. I will also report to the Central Government on the recent situation in Shanxi on behalf of Commissioner Yan. I will also take the opportunity to discuss matters such as Central Government's financial assistance to the Shanxi military. I will not be leaving Beijing and returning north in the short term." I asked how Commissioner Yan views the overall situation. Zhao replied that Commissioner Yan sincerely hopes that everyone will unite to resist foreign aggression. Yan previously returned to Hebian Village to care for his father, who was ill. He has now recovered, so he has returned to Taiyuan. Zhang Qun recently went to Taiyuan from Pingjin and met with Yan several times. He has now returned to Hankou. Regarding the overall situation in North China, the Central Government probably has concrete plans. I asked about the military pay of the various armies in Shanxi. He replied that the Central Government had previously promised to provide 600,000 yuan per month to Shanxi, but due to financial difficulties, it has not been allocated. As for the guest armies, such as those of Sun Dianying, Song Zheyuan, and Pang Bingxun, Director Zhang (Xueliang) provided some financial assistance each month during the period of the Beiping Pacification Office. Zhang Renjie and Bao Gang's armies raised funds locally. The original armies stationed in Shanxi were supplied by the provincial government. After the establishment of the Taiyuan Pacification Office, its powers were divided with the Beiping Pacification Office, and the Central Government promised to provide another 100,000 yuan per month to the Shanxi armies, but it has also not been allocated. Because Shanxi is poor and has financial difficulties, I am going to Beijing this time to request the Central Government to expedite the allocation. I asked about the recent floods in Shanxi. Zhao replied that the Fen River flooded this year, and 30 or 40 counties along the river were affected. It was partial, not completely flooded. The southern gate of Taiyuan was also flooded due to the breaching of the Fen River dam. When the floodwaters rose, the garrisoned troops in the city closed the city gates to prevent flooding, fortunately avoiding being flooded. Previously, a few counties in southern Shanxi had a widespread tiger plague, but it has now subsided somewhat. I asked where the remnants of Liu Guitang's bandits are currently operating. He replied that the remnants of Liu Guitang's bandits were previously in the Ling Shou area on the border of Shanxi and Hebei. They never entered Shanxi. They have now moved to the Chahar-Suiyuan area. There are few bandits in Shanxi. It is quite peaceful. (September 13th)

Bandit Situation in Anhui Province Gradually Being Eliminated 6

Anqing Correspondence: The bandit forces of Quan Guangyi and Zhang Da-bizi in Anhui Province, after merging, disturbed the areas of Tongcheng and Lujiang. The provincial government sent the police second brigade, Ni Regiment, to join the Tongcheng, Lujiang, and Shu counties militias to suppress them. Later, it was decided to request support from the 33rd Brigade, led by Brigade Commander Tang Yunshan, and sent a regiment of troops to assist. Tang also went to command. The original plan was to encircle and annihilate them, but the strength of the militias near the Chaohu Lake in Lujiang was somewhat weak, so the bandits fled in that direction. The Ni Regiment is currently pursuing them. The Tang Brigade has advanced to Lujiang, approaching the border of Shucheng County. Yesterday, the provincial government received a telegram from Xiong Gonglie of Tongcheng, stating that Zhang's bandits, after fleeing north from Shaxi, were closely pursued by the Ni Regiment to the vicinity of Pingdingshan in Forty Forts, where they engaged in fierce fighting. The Tang Brigade had set out from Dongtangchi on the 8th, preparing to launch a head-on attack. As for the Shucheng area, Liang Guanying, the commander-in-chief of the 25th Route Army, telegraphed the provincial government, stating that the Zheng and Liu Brigades of the route army had successively recovered Jiugongzhai, Lianghekou, Heishidu, Daxiao Yiling, Xindianhe, Bangedian, and other places, and were currently eliminating the remaining bandits and resettling the displaced. Provincial Chairman Wu Zhongxin has sent a telegram of commendation. As for the Liuan area, Wang Jun also telegraphed the provincial government, stating that the Red bandits had been repeatedly defeated and had concentrated their forces to retreat and defend Mabou. The 19th, 21st, and 33rd Brigades were deployed to advance on Xianghuling, Shajiawan, and other places, breaking through the first and second lines of defense of the bandit area, engaging in day and night hand-to-hand combat, and completely recovering Mabou. Several thousand bandits were killed in this battle. The units are now attacking Majialing, Yangjiadian, and other places. Jinjiazai has been surrounded and will be captured soon. As for the sporadic small bandits in Tongcheng and Wuwei, the provincial government has also sent the Wang Battalion of the first regiment of the second police brigade and Liao Yunze, the chief of the first section of the Security Office, to the Liujiadu, Xiang'an, and Huanggutun areas to search and suppress them. (September 14th)

Western Journey Notes (22) 7

Only Two and a Half Portions of Life

"Riding a horse or sailing a boat is only worth three portions of life," but the danger of riding in a "jiawo" (a type of covered litter) from Fushi to Ganguyu is only worth two and a half portions of life. These were the heartfelt words of Liu Chenghou, Deputy Director of the North Group, when he arrived at the Ganguyu residence at 5:00 PM on August 30th. Indeed, the road that day (the 30th) was not particularly difficult, but the experiences of each person were extremely dangerous. I still remember that day, at 7:30 AM, our donkeys, horses, and "jiawo" carriages, swaying and swaggering, marched out of Fushi city gate in a grand manner. In less than three or four minutes, one of the donkeys pulling my "jiawo" carriage suddenly started dancing as if it were listening to music in the Shanghai La Fei Garden. I felt that something was amiss and immediately got out of the "jiawo" to walk. However, Mr. Huang Bokui, a mining magnate with profound feelings, insisted on exchanging places with me. I could not refuse out of politeness and had to agree. Unexpectedly, both the front and rear donkeys pulling the "jiawo" started dancing simultaneously midway. The "jiawo" carriage immediately overturned. Onlookers were very worried for Mr. Huang, but fortunately, he was not injured. At 1:00 PM, after our break at Shiyaodianzi (resting place) was over, the "jiawo" carriage of Feng Huanzhang, a councilor of the Shaanxi Provincial Government, was crossing the river when the "jiawo" carriage reached the middle of the stream. The front donkey and the following donkey did not cooperate, and the front donkey broke away from the "jiawo" and went its own way. Mr. Feng almost fell into the water and was in great danger. In addition to this, Mr. Zhu Jierui fell from his horse and injured his foot severely. Although he asked the group doctor, Mr. Hu Tingyu, to treat him, he still looked like an iron-crutch immortal when he walked.

Ganguyu was just an overnight stop between Fushi and Yanchang. Because Fushi and Yanchang are 160 "li" apart, and we only traveled eighty or ninety "li" each day, we stayed overnight in a small school in Ganguyu. The next morning (the 31st), when we got up to hit the road, everyone was on guard. Therefore, when the donkeys pulling the "jiawo" carriages reached the edge of the cliffs, they also felt the urge to dance. Then our lives would be in danger. For a time, the number of people abandoning the "jiawo" carriages and walking increased significantly. Sure enough, midway, the "jiawo" carriage of the agriculturalist, Mr. Li Yongxing, suddenly did a 180-degree flip. The contents of the boxes were scattered all over the place in the most vivid detail. Fortunately, Mr. Li had already joined the walkers and escaped this disaster. Otherwise, he would have at least grazed some skin on his forehead and suffered a false alarm.

After breaking at Heijiabao at 12:00 PM, most of us believed that the overturned "jiawo" carriages were a warning and decided to walk. However, the mountains stood tall and steep, and the roadsides were full of stone slabs, making it difficult to walk. We desperately pushed forward and, after about an hour, ran to Xihazigou. Because the river was dry, the water flow was only as narrow as a line. We walked in the riverbed, so it felt relatively smooth. At 3:30 PM, we saw a solitary city in the distance, suddenly appearing before our eyes. We knew that we had arrived at Yanchang, which has long been famous for its oil.

Since we left Xi'an, we have kept accurate records of the altitude, temperature, and climate of various places. Now that we have passed the halfway point of our journey, I will copy out the records for reference:

Location Date Altitude Temperature Climate

Same as above August 17th Same as above 26 degrees Celsius Rain

Same as above August 19th Same as above Same as above Sunny

Summary of Important News 9

Therefore, many difficulties were felt. The daily progress is briefly described below for the reference of those who are concerned about the Northwest.

On August 15th, the group departed from Xi'an and traveled 50 "li" south, spending the night in a place called "Yinjiahui." The entire route was flat, but due to the prolonged lack of rain, the farmland was barren, and nine out of ten villages were empty. It was truly unbearable to witness. However, the closer to Yinjiahui, the denser the trees in the villages became, and seedlings could occasionally be seen in the low-lying areas. This was because the closer to the mountains, the greater the rainfall and the slightly higher the humidity. The severity of the tiger epidemic in Yinjiahui was unprecedented. The town had a population of no more than a thousand people, but the daily death toll from the epidemic was no less than thirty people. It was common for several people to die in the same room, and it was not uncommon for entire families to die from the epidemic. The people only engaged in praying to gods and did not pay attention to hygiene to seek preventive methods. It was truly pitiful. Even among the members of our group, no fewer than ten soldiers and laborers contracted the epidemic that day. Fortunately, the group members were all unharmed, except for Dr. Ye.

On August 16th, the group traveled 15 "li" south from Yinjiahui and entered the Qinling Mountains through "Dashizui." The group traveled 60 "li" in the mountains and spent the night in Banmiao. The section from Yinjiahui to Dashizui was still flat. The mountains were close, and the water was abundant, making irrigation easy. Therefore, rice paddies and cornfields were often a patch of green, which was truly a rare sight after entering Tongguan. However, the ferocity of the tigers in each village was no less than in Yinjiahui. After entering the mountains from Dashizui, the number of people living in the mountains has greatly increased in recent years, and the forests have been completely destroyed. Forest land has been converted into farmland. The mountains twisted and turned, with a bend every five steps and a turn every ten steps. The mountain streams wound through the mountains, which was truly spectacular. Therefore, what pleased the members was the scenery, but what troubled the members were their legs. When the group reached Banmiao in the evening, the weather gradually cooled, and it was impossible to keep warm without cotton-padded clothing.

On August 17th, the group set off from Banmiao and traveled 30 "li" south, crossing the 8,000-foot-high Qinling Mountains, and then traveled more than 30 "li" down the south side of the mountains, spending the night in Sanliqiao. In the areas traversed that day, the residents gradually became sparse, and the forests became denser. Unknowingly, we had entered the mountainous climate. At this time of year, the rain was not heavy but continuous, and the clouds were not shallow, often causing inconvenience to travelers. There was a Han Yu Temple on the ridge, which was truly as Su Shi said, "The spirit of the Duke is like water in the ground, everywhere." When the group reached Sanliqiao, many members went to the "natural pool" in the mountain stream to take a soda bath that did not cost a penny, which was truly a pleasure on the journey. At the meeting in the evening, it was learned that one soldier and five laborers from our group had died from the epidemic in the past two days. A sorrowful atmosphere suddenly appeared in the meeting place.

On August 18th, the group set off from Sanliqiao and went south along the Ganyou River, passing through Yingpanzhen and traveling 80 "li", spending the night in Shizuizi, five "li" south of Zhashui County. When the group passed through Yingpanzhen, the people feared that we would bring the epidemic from the north of the mountains to the south of the mountains, so they burned weeds to drive away the plague. So we had become plague gods. When the group passed through Zhashui County, we saw slogans posted all over the streets to welcome the survey group. The slogans included "The Shaanxi Industrial Survey Group is the Pioneer of Northwest Development," etc. The most bizarre slogan was "Welcome the China Science Society to Drive Away the Plague," etc.

On August 19th, the group stopped in Shizuizi for a day, and held a discussion meeting with the county magistrate, the director of the Construction Bureau, and the representatives of the legal entities to make a county-wide survey and statistics.

On August 20th, the group set off from Shizuizi. In addition to the main group traveling south along the Ganyou River, passing through Guta Temple and arriving in Zhen'an County at noon the next day (the 21st), Professor Li Deyi organized a detachment to explore the local cup industry situation through the Yungaisi mountain road. The detachment also arrived in Zhen'an at noon on the 21st and rejoined the main group. The main group, led by Director Hu Shuhua, investigated the local copper mines in various places, collected samples, and waited for analysis and testing. The forest conditions of the small roads passed by the detachment were indeed better than in other places. If large-scale mining were considered, it would not be very economical. Residents mostly planted oak trees, and the quantity was considerable. When the group arrived in Zhen'an County, slogans and national flags were seen all over the streets, and the wording was the same as in Zhashui. In the evening, a lengthy discussion was held with the county magistrate and representatives of various legal entities until 12:00 AM, when everyone dispersed happily.

On the morning of August 22nd, the group set off from Zhen'an and traveled south, passing through Qingtongzha, Xiheguan, and Mapinghe, totaling 360 "li", and arrived in Ankang County on the evening of the 25th. The travel experience during these four days is summarized as follows:

(A) The mountain roads were difficult and dangerous. The daily journey in the traversed areas was long, and the mountains were even more dangerous. The roads traveled were mostly small paths along the river, which were only a foot or so wide. An accidental misstep would lead to no chance of survival. Take the 40 "li" journey from Xiheguan by boat to Zhaojiawan as an example. It was extremely dangerous. The water flow was rapid and shallow, and the bottom of the boat rubbed against the river stones, making a sound. In the rapids, the bow of the boat often ran the risk of colliding with the rocks on the shore. Fortunately, the group members were adventurous and had no difficulties. (B) Fortunately, the group did not encounter bandits. Although the group had escaped the threat of the tiger epidemic, there was still concern about bandits in the dangerous mountains all day long. The group's travel procedures were therefore appropriately improved and prepared for any eventuality. Fortunately, there were no accidents, which was comforting to the families of the group members.

(C) The problem of planting mountains. Opening up mountain slopes for planting is a phenomenon of population increase. More than half of the mountains that the group passed through had already been opened up for planting. The remaining uncultivated areas were either because they had been cultivated and could no longer be farmed, or because they were too rocky to be cultivated. If this continued without finding a remedy, the amount of mountain land would decrease, while the population would increase. After several decades, this would truly be a major problem in the area.

On the evening of the twenty-fifth, when the group arrived in Ankang County, Commander Zhang Feisheng personally came to the suburbs to greet them. By the time they entered the city, thousands of homes were lit up, slogans covered the walls, national flags fluttered in the wind, and military music was played. The grandeur here was no less than when the group departed from Xi'an. From August 26th, the group stayed in Ankang for two days. On the morning of the 26th, they rested, and in the afternoon, they attended a banquet hosted by Commander Zhang Feisheng. In the evening, they talked with the county magistrate and various legal entities. At 5:00 AM on the 27th, Commander Zhang invited the group members to review the troops and talk to the soldiers. At noon, they attended a banquet hosted by various legal entities, and local operas were performed for entertainment. In the afternoon, the group members went to the suburbs and various shops to investigate everything. The most bizarre thing was that a few people even regarded the group as if they were imperial envoys. Some asked the group to reduce miscellaneous taxes, and some accused local tyrants and evil gentry. It is estimated that they did not understand the group's mission, which was also pitiful. Ankang County is located on the south bank of the Han River and is a major thoroughfare for transporting goods from Hanzhong to Hankou. In the past, business was quite prosperous. In 1923, the value of exported goods exceeded 5 million yuan. There were dozens of large businesses. Now, due to the unstable situation and the difficulty of the waterway to Hankou, it has become a dying market with nine out of ten doors closed. It is hoped that the authorities will pay close attention to the Han River transportation in Hubei Province. (Recorded at the Seventh Middle School in the west of Ankang City on August 27th)

Extension of the Longhai Railway to the East Section 10

Jiangsu Province Plans Commercial Port Locations

The eastern extension of the Longhai Railway is expected to open to traffic to Xugou by the end of this year. In the spring of next year, after the Sunjiashan Tunnel is completed, it can open to traffic to Laoyao, and a wharf will be built there. It is expected to be completed in two or three months. At the 528th meeting of the Jiangsu Provincial Government yesterday, regarding the Longhai Railway Bureau's plan to set up commercial areas in Xugou, Laoyao, and other places along the route, the locations for establishing commercial ports were planned in detail. It was resolved to have the four departments of Civil Affairs, Finance, Construction, and Industry jointly review the plan, which would be convened by the Construction Department. This type of construction is extremely important to the prosperity of northern Jiangsu. The original letter from the Longhai Railway Bureau to the Jiangsu Provincial Government is recorded as follows: "Regarding the construction of a wharf by this bureau in Xugou, the situation has been reported to your government in previous letters. The survey procedures are nearing completion, and the earthwork and stonework of the roadbed have already begun. It is expected that traffic to Xugou can open by the end of this year. In the spring of next year, after the Sunjiashan Tunnel is completed, traffic can open to Laoyao, and the wharf there will also be completed and open for transport in two or three months. At this time, there will inevitably be many travelers and merchants coming and going, but it is necessary to have the facilities for hotels and warehouses to accommodate them. However, the area around Xugou is extremely remote, with few villages. If the government designates the commercial area in advance and plans for the safety of land and water in advance, merchants will not be suspicious and will naturally be eager to invest and engage in construction. Your government has far-sighted vision and strives for construction. All of these facilities must have been planned in detail to meet the expectations of the people. The railway and the local area are an integrated whole, sharing weal and woe. Has your government considered designating the location for the establishment of a commercial port, or is it anticipated when it can be opened? Please provide detailed information so that the railway administration can also promote it at the same time and share the optimistic success."

Kunshan 11

A cotton-picking incident led to a fatal case. Zhu, the wife of a plasterer named Chen Aqiao, and A Da, his daughter-in-law, of Yu Xiang Village, Shipu Township, Kunshan County, had a quarrel with a farmer named Song Xiaohu from a neighboring village over cotton picking the day before yesterday evening. First, they cursed and scolded, and then Chen and the other two twisted Song and beat him fiercely. Zhu kicked Song hard in the arm, causing a serious injury that resulted in immediate death. Seeing that a disaster had occurred, the villagers detained Chen and the other two and sent them to the local security team, who transferred them to the Qian Dun Public Security Bureau for detention. On the 12th, they were sent to the county government for legal action, and a request was made to send personnel for inspection. On the 13th, County Magistrate Cheng commissioned the Chen trial investigator to go with the inspection official to investigate. It was found that the deceased had been kicked in the kidney and testicles during his lifetime, resulting in death. The body was placed in a coffin by the family, and a summons was issued for verification.

The detective team captured bandits in Shanghai. Qin Jieren, the director of the Kunshan County Public Security Bureau, received a tip that dozens of bandits from Anhui were colluding in Shanghai, planning to kidnap someone in a certain township in this county. Upon receiving the report, Director Qin immediately ordered the detective team leader Quan Lin to go to Shanghai to cooperate with the Shanghai-based investigator Pan Hongshou, and dispatched police from the First Precinct of the Fourth District to capture four bandits, including Zai Shuqing, Chen Yunting, Chen Yongqing, and Xi Huazhai, in the Yi Dai Jiao area. Three pistols and twenty-three bullets were seized. Subsequently, Director Qin prepared a document to Shanghai and escorted the four criminals back to Kunshan at 5:00 PM on the 13th. They were sent to the county government for interrogation.

The eighth district chief was accused. Jin Deji, the eighth district chief of this county, has been in office for three years. Recently, local gentry Wu Renjie, Xu Liang, Qu Zuzheng, Zhou Tiandu, Gao Bangjun, Zhao Jingyi, Xie Jingxiu, and others jointly filed a complaint with the Kunshan County Government and the Jiangsu Provincial Civil Affairs Department, accusing District Chief Jin of privately and arbitrarily imposing fines, demolishing ancient tombs, abusing private individuals, monopolizing public property, squandering public funds, embezzling public goods, and neglecting public health, etc. Wu and others also came to Shanghai yesterday to convene fellow villagers to report on the case and requested fellow villagers to uphold justice to maintain local politics.

Changing the Method of Accepting Mortgaged Silkworm Cocoons and Reorganizing Jiangsu and Zhejiang Factories

The Silk and Silkworm Cocoon Committee previously stipulated the method for cleaning up old silkworm cocoons. Anyone who transported old silkworm cocoons from warehouses to factories for silk reeling, whether their own cocoons or commissioned silk reeling, should report to the committee in writing in advance, and a certificate would be issued after the investigation stock confirmed that there were no errors. Now, the deadline for the export subsidy for old silk is approaching, with only four months left until the end of the year, and the relationship between the mortgaged funds and the pledged funds is extremely important. It is necessary to strive for convenience in terms of procedures. The method has been changed. In the future, if old silkworm cocoons are to be shipped to warehouse owners, the cargo owner may request a certificate from the warehouse stating the number of the warehouse receipt, the number of packages shipped, and the date of shipment, and send it directly to the committee to issue a silk reeling certificate. Yesterday, the Shanghai, Zhejiang, and Wuxi Silk Factories Association was notified to inform the factories to check and handle.

Since the written warning was ineffective, members were dispatched to assassinate him unsuccessfully and fired a shot as a demonstration, etc.

Xiaoshan 18

Unemployed Worker Commits Suicide Due to Poverty and Illness. Yu Qiuchen, a worker from Shalang Yu, a village in the western suburbs of Xiaoshan, used to work as a deputy foreman at the Qingcheng Silk Factory in Hangzhou. He lost his job and returned home when the factory shut down due to the current economic downturn. After months of being unemployed, his savings were completely exhausted. He contracted typhoid fever last month and has yet to recover. His family of five, including the elderly and the young, had no means of livelihood, and Yu was heavily in debt. Unable to cope with the creditors during the Mid-Autumn Festival, he became despondent and hanged himself on the twelfth day at midnight. By the time his family found him, he was already dead. This morning, his 70-year-old mother also attempted suicide by throwing herself into the pond behind the house, but fortunately, a neighbor noticed her and rescued her from drowning. It was a fortunate event.

Gaoyou 19

Unable to Get Through the Holiday Season, He Hanged Himself. Chen Changle, a farmer from Gantuo Township, Ninth District of the county, inherited over 60 acres of farmland, which was enough to make a living. However, in recent years, due to successive crop failures, life became difficult, and he had to borrow money to survive. Since the beginning of summer this year, due to severe drought, the autumn harvest was poor. With the Mid-Autumn Festival approaching and creditors knocking on his door, Chen became despondent. He took advantage of his family's sound sleep the night before, sneaked out of the house, and hanged himself on a windmill. When his family discovered him the next morning, he was already dead. It was a tragic event.

Special Education News

Problems in Elementary School Moral Education (Part 2) by Wu Zengjie 20

2. How to Cultivate Good Behavior in Children: Moral education is not about filling students' minds with moral concepts, but about expressing these concepts and ideals. We need to see if they understand the meaning of morality by observing whether they can act according to moral principles. Based on this understanding, elementary school moral education is not just empty lectures on moral precepts or the organization of children's self-governance societies with a few leaders in charge. True moral education requires every student to share in the work of collective activities, and every child to have a sense of responsibility. All kinds of activities within the reach of children's abilities, such as publishing news, maintaining order, and managing libraries, should be done in rotation by students of all grades. In this way, universal training can be achieved, breaking the old pattern of a few people being active and the majority being passive.

3. How to Guide Children: The only methods generally used in elementary schools to guide children's behavior are "good deeds must be rewarded, and bad deeds must be punished." Good students receive many prizes at the end of the semester and are very happy, while bad students are punished with hard labor, "detention," loud scolding, and even corporal punishment. Are rewards and punishments the best methods? Encouraging with prizes easily fosters pride, while punishment can cause children to resent teachers and lose faith in them. Should rewards and punishments be used? What methods can replace them? These questions need to be studied. Teachers should have a broad vision when guiding children and should consider all aspects. They should not be bound by preconceived notions. They should know that naughty students are not necessarily useless people, and those who follow the rules are not necessarily talented. Teachers should also pay attention to the difference between liveliness and naughtiness.

4. How to Improve Society: Many bad habits of children can be said to be learned from adults. Not to mention other things, let's take cleanliness and order as examples. Elementary school students hear their teachers talk about the importance of cleanliness and order almost every day at school. But as soon as they leave school and go to the streets, they find it dirty and noisy everywhere. Children feel that emphasizing cleanliness and order is only a matter within the school. Outside the school, because everyone is like that, they can be casual. With this kind of mentality, what effect can school moral education have? Elementary school teachers should know that moral education cannot be successfully done by closing the school gates. To have children with good behavior, it must start with adults. Therefore, elementary school teachers must take on the work of adult education. Only by educating adults well can they train children with greater success. If adult education is abandoned and only children's training is emphasized, it will be a case of doing twice the work with half the results.

5. How to Connect with Families: To make moral education effective, it is also necessary to connect with families. Parents and teachers are jointly responsible for children's training, but in reality, parents' attitudes toward children and teachers' attitudes toward children cannot be consistent. Parents may not know how to guide children, some are too strict, some are too lenient, and some fathers and mothers have inconsistent attitudes toward children. These phenomena make school moral education difficult. Elementary school teachers should do more home visits. We should go to accommodate the parents, not sit in the school and wait for the parents to come, or hold entertainment programs, ostensibly called "parent-teacher conferences," and think that we have done the work of connection.

Due to limited space, this article ends here. There are many problems in elementary school moral education, and teachers must pay attention to improvement at all times. I would like to share this with my colleagues in the elementary school education community.

Annual Meeting of the Chinese Economic Society

Fifth Preparatory Meeting Held Yesterday

Local News

Feng Yong University Reopens in Beiping 22

Plans to Recruit Male and Female Students in Shanghai on a Set Date

In the spring of the 16th year of the Republic (1927), Feng Yong of Liaoning opened up 102,000 acres of land and founded Feng Yong University on the Hun River. Established for four years, the school achieved remarkable results, with three colleges and nine departments, comprehensive facilities, and strict discipline. After the September 18th Incident (Mukden Incident), the entire school was destroyed, suffering losses of millions. Currently, the school site has been moved to the old Army University in Beiping, and efforts are being made to reopen the school. On the 21st and 22nd of this month, the school will recruit first-year students for the university's political science, education, and physical education departments, as well as sophomore-level students in education, and students at all levels of high school and junior high school, at the Wuben Girls' Middle School in Ximen, Shanghai. The total cost per semester is 49 yuan for university, 43 yuan for high school, and 27 yuan for junior high school. The registration period is from now until the 20th. It is heard that the school's principle for students is kindness and freedom of belief, while strictly prohibiting political party activities. Students are subject to absolute discipline in group life. Separate admission guidelines are available for each examination subject and can be obtained from the Feng Da Admissions Committee at Wuben Girls' Middle School.

The Twentieth Army's Last Battle 29

Lost 4-0 to the Municipal First Team

The Twentieth Army football team visited the Songhu war zone today and played a basketball game with the refereeing association in the evening. They will leave Shanghai for Hangzhou tomorrow. Therefore, yesterday afternoon's football match with the Municipal First Sports Field team was their last battle. According to the record of the Twentieth Army football team's performance in Shanghai, wins and losses were mixed, neither profitable nor unprofitable. Therefore, yesterday's game was quite related to the team's overall account. However, the Municipal First Army had a tough attitude, continued their efforts, and developed a one-sided situation, winning 4-0, which was quite unexpected. The battle situation is recorded as follows:

After the lower team Shuwei Yinjiao sounded, the two armies formed their positions, intending to attack. The Municipal First Center forward first passed the ball, and the left and right armies communicated and passed it, reaching the Sichuan army's penalty area, like a gust of wind and rain. Left forward Huang Guorong got the ball in a hurry and shot against the momentum. The ball immediately went into the net, killing a power display, in less than two minutes.

Shooting from afar at the gate, preparing for the battle, the Municipal First's arrogance increased, but the Sichuan army did not show weakness. Left forward Ma Zuyin was particularly brave and active, but the Municipal First left midfielder Ding Zhaocheng watched him very closely, and the hero had almost no place to use his skills. Since the Municipal First's front army had no worries about internal defense, they bravely attacked directly. The Sichuan army welcomed and rejected them separately, and the position gradually became chaotic. The Municipal First left inside player Fu Zhibin shot a ball from afar, directly penetrating the gate, making the score 2-0.

Scoring three consecutive goals, the Sichuan army suffered a setback, and their momentum declined slightly, while the Municipal First's front army's attack became more urgent. Center Chen Liang, left and right midfielders Yang Guozhen and Ding Zhaocheng all crossed the gap and welcomed and sent each other according to the opportunity. In a short time, the Municipal First Army was again in the Sichuan Army's penalty area, rushing from left to right. As a result, Wang Boyong got the supply from Cao Qiuting and turned around to sweep and shoot, scoring three goals in a row.

The Sichuan army worked hard. After the Sichuan army suffered heavy losses, they worked hard to attack fiercely. Liu Ximeng led the three armies, came in a long drive, and surrounded the three sides. Suddenly, a ball flew straight to the upper left corner of the Municipal First's goal. Goalkeeper Wang Jingen jumped and grabbed it, kicked it out, and the crisis passed.

Unfeeling feet, after the lemon, Municipal First left inside guard Zheng Zhiyun came on the field, united with Lu Yongxi, the wall was more solid, and the Sichuan army's momentum was even more depressed, and within the territory, it was often trampled by the Municipal First Army. In this situation of being besieged on all sides, Mai Youliang's feet were unfeeling, and he took the opportunity of a corner kick to score another goal.

Close to dusk, the battle was mixed. At this time, it was dusk, and the color was vast. The Sichuan army defended with all its strength and had no intention of attacking, and the critical situation had not diminished slightly. Blocking from the left and right, it was extremely chaotic. Three penalty kicks were not hit, which can also be said to be fortunate.

"Theory and Method of Elementary School Physical Education" by Chen Kuisheng, Expert in Elementary and Secondary School Physical Education 31

| Published Today |

"Morning Exercises and Interval Exercises" Co-authored by Jin Zhaojun and Chen Kuisheng Also Published

Chen Kuisheng, an expert in physical education in elementary and secondary schools, has lectured on "Theory and Method of Elementary School Physical Education" at teachers' colleges, physical education schools, and Tsinghua University summer physical education workshops for more than ten years, totaling twenty-eight times. This summer, he represented Hunan Province at the National Sports Conference and was invited to lecture on elementary school physical education at the Shanghai Education Bureau's summer lecture series. Listeners all admired him. Now, Mr. Chen's "Theory and Method of Elementary School Physical Education" is published today. The book is divided into eighteen chapters: Chapter 1, The Importance of Elementary School Physical Education; Chapter 2, The Position of Physical Education in Education; Chapter 3, The Physique and Nature of Children in Elementary School; Chapter 4, The Purpose of Elementary School Physical Education; Chapter 5, The Classification of Physical Education Movements and Their Effects and Disadvantages; Chapter 6, Physical Education Training That Should Be Implemented in Elementary Schools; Chapter 7, Games; Chapter 8, Track and Field; Chapter 9, Walking; Chapter 10, Soft Gymnastics; Chapter 11, Apparatus Gymnastics; Chapter 12, Dancing; Chapter 13, Martial Arts; Chapter 14, Examination Posture; Chapter 15, Elementary School Hygiene Curriculum Standards and Examination Methods; Chapter 16, A Study of Elementary School Physical Education Curriculum Standards and Teaching Time Allocation; Chapter 17, A Discussion on the Examination of Elementary School Physical Education Achievements; Chapter 18, The Organizational Law of Elementary School Sports Meets. The book also includes hundreds of illustrations. Elementary school physical education teachers need not worry about the lack of teaching materials with this book. Physical education schools can use it as a textbook. The entire book is a thick volume, beautifully printed. For the sake of popularization, it is sold for only one dollar and seventy cents, with a special price of 10% off. The postage fee for mail orders is sixteen cents. In addition, "Morning Exercises and Interval Exercises," co-authored by Mr. Chen and Jin Zhaojun, a physical education professor at Central University, is also very valuable and published today. It details the implementation methods of morning exercises and interval exercises and includes teaching materials. It is a must-have book for elementary and secondary school physical education teachers. The price is fifty cents per copy, with a special price of 10% off. The postage fee for mail orders is nine cents. The above two books are two new types of physical education series published by Qinfen Bookstore, Huajinli Port, No. 4 Road, Shanghai.

Zhejiang Province to Hold Regular Sports Meets 32

To Be Held in Four Zones in October

The third Zhejiang Provincial Games were originally planned to be held last autumn, but they could not be held due to lack of funds. Now, the Department of Education has decided to divide the province into four major zones and hold them separately. The preparatory directors have been appointed. The first zone, Hangzhou, Jiaxing, and Huzhou, will be prepared by Ye Suzong, the principal of the provincial high school; the second zone, Ningbo, Shaoxing, and Taizhou, will be prepared by Shen Qida, the principal of the Fourth High School; the third zone, Jinhua, Quzhou, and Yan'an, will be prepared by Zui Fanghao, the principal of the Seventh High School; and the fourth zone, Wenzhou and Chuzhou, will be prepared by Zhang Hao, the principal of the Tenth High School. All secondary schools and above in the entire zone, regardless of whether they are provincial or private, must participate. The funding regulation is 600 yuan per zone, with the Department of Education subsidizing half of it, and the rest will be shared by the participating schools. The date is set in October, with the first Saturday as the holding period for the first zone, and the second zone will be held on the following Saturday. In terms of events, group exercises, health competitions, scout performances, and swimming and ball games will be added in accordance with the second session's method. The provincial games will be held next spring.

Local News

Song Ziwen and Chen Gongbo Talk

The Central Government Decides to Suppress the Puppet Organization

The National Government Has Already Decided on a Concrete Plan

A Clear Order Will Be Issued After the Publication of the League of Nations Report

A Protest Has Been Lodged with Japan and a Note Has Been Sent to the Washington Treaty Countries

According to the Central News Agency, after the Japanese Privy Council formally approved the recognition of the puppet organization, the central government decided not only to lodge a stern protest with Japan but also to invoke the Nine-Power Treaty to draw the attention of the signatory countries to Japan's invasion of the Northeast and its blatant disregard for everything by formally recognizing the puppet organization. A reporter from the Central News Agency visited Song Ziwen, the acting president of the Executive Yuan, at his residence yesterday to inquire whether the National Government would issue an order to suppress the puppet organization immediately after Japan announced its recognition of the puppet organization on the 15th. According to Song, the suppression of the puppet organization is not because Japan recognizes it. All rebels must be suppressed. The National Government is determined to suppress the puppet organization in the Northeast. According to Chen Gongbo, the Minister of Industry, the central government has already decided on a concrete plan for suppressing the puppet organization in the Northeast. The reason for the discussion at yesterday's Executive Yuan meeting was that the League of Nations hoped not to complicate the Northeast problem before the publication of the investigation report. Therefore, the National Government's clear order to suppress may be issued after the publication of the League of Nations investigation report. As for Japan's absurd move, it clearly violates the Nine-Power Treaty. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs will lodge a serious protest and send a note to the signatory countries of the treaty, asking them to pay special attention.

Upholding Justice and Maintaining Conventions

Sanction Japan for Recognizing the Puppet State

The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, the Shanghai Banking Association, and the Shanghai Money Trade Association sent two telegrams yesterday regarding Japan's recognition of the Manchurian puppet state: (1) Minister Luo and Vice Minister Liu of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Nanjing, please forward to the Secretariat of the League of Nations in Geneva. Japan's recognition of the Manchurian puppet state further proves the destruction of China's territorial sovereignty and integrity. Our country strongly opposes this. We hope that you will uphold justice, uphold conventions, and quickly impose sanctions to maintain world peace. The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce of China, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, the Shanghai Banking Association, and the Shanghai Money Trade Association respectfully kowtow. (2) Sent to the Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, the Executive Yuan, and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Nanjing. Japan's recognition of the puppet state further proves the destruction of our country's territorial sovereignty and integrity. The affiliated associations have jointly telegraphed the League of Nations, requesting sanctions. We earnestly request a strict protest and hope that the whole country will unite and fight against foreign enemies to save the country from danger. We are waiting for orders. The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce of China, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, the Shanghai Banking Association, and the Shanghai Money Trade Association respectfully kowtow.

The Tragic September 18th 35

City Government Dispatches Police for Prevention

Chamber of Commerce Announces Half-Mast Flags

The anniversary of the September 18th National Humiliation is approaching, and coupled with Japan's open recognition of the puppet organization, compatriots across the country will undoubtedly feel even more grief. The municipal authorities are deeply concerned that excessive public outrage may lead to excessive actions, necessitating precautions. All sectors have decided to hold mourning ceremonies on that day. The situation is recorded as follows:

The Municipal Government Expresses its View: A reporter from Xin Sheng News Agency went to the municipal government yesterday to inquire about the prevention measures for the September 18th commemoration. According to the person in charge of the municipal government, if the commemoration of September 18th in this city can be carried out with calm and solemn actions amidst grief and fervor, there is no need for prevention. However, it is inevitable that hot-blooded youths and patriotic people may become overly激動 and exceed the limits, leading to disturbances. At the same time, reactionary elements taking the opportunity to make trouble is also a concern. Therefore, in order to maintain order, police force will be increased and strict precautions will be taken before and after September 18th, so that the entire city can commemorate in an orderly manner and avoid unexpected events. As for the Japanese newspapers' reports that 5,000 troops have been added in the Zhenru area and that our country is actively purchasing military equipment for conflict with Japan, these are all deliberate attempts by Japanese news to provoke feelings between the two countries and make the situation worse. In fact, no troops have been added to this city. At this time of international turbulence, it is truly regrettable that the Japanese newspapers suddenly have such inaccurate news reports.

Chamber of Commerce Notice: The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce yesterday issued a notice to all industry associations and store members in the city, stating that the Shenyang Incident will soon be a year old, and the three northeastern provinces have fallen into foreign hands. All of our citizens should emulate themselves with unwavering determination to avoid the pain of China's downfall. Therefore, the entire city is gathered, and the Youth Propaganda Team is borrowed to hold a National Humiliation Commemoration Meeting on the morning of September 18th at 9:00 AM. It is hoped that all industry associations will send two representatives to attend the meeting at that time. All stores in the city should also fly flags at half-mast for one day to express the grief of the entire country.

Fasting to Express Sorrow: Since the September 18th Incident, the Chinese Vocational Education Society has done its utmost for practical national salvation work. Recently, it launched a monthly donation campaign based on salary size to support the Northeast Volunteer Army, with the aim of sustaining the resistance force. The movement in this city has been vigorous, and the accumulated amount is quite considerable. Yesterday, the society received a telegram from representatives of various national salvation organizations in Beiping, Yan Baohang and Cha Liangzhao, which stated that the local organizations proposed a national noon fasting on September 18th to express the determination to recover lost territory. Various organizations, schools, institutions, families, and individuals should voluntarily hand over the saved meal expenses to local trust institutions, banks, or newspapers for collection and remittance to the Shanghai Northeast Refugee Relief Association to help the suffering compatriots in the Northeast. It is requested that this be promoted in Shanghai to promote public spirit. After discussion, all expressed their support. Those who signed up to join included Huang Renzhi, Liu Zhanen, Jiang Wenyu, Yang Weiyu, Yao Huiquan, etc., all the staff of the headquarters, and personnel from various affiliated institutions, totaling more than a thousand people. The noon meal expenses saved at that time will be approximately over one hundred yuan, which will be given to the Northeast Refugee Relief Association.

Before and After September 18th 36

Japanese Troops Stationed in Shanghai on Alert

After the Japanese government announced its recognition of the puppet organization, the Japanese military and political authorities in this city, with the approaching of September 18th, were increasingly afraid of arousing resentment among the Chinese people, so they became more actively on alert. The details are recorded separately as follows:

Armored Vehicles Deployed in Two Locations: The Japanese Shanghai Daily News published on the evening of the 14th that the Japanese Marine Corps stationed in Shanghai, with the impending recognition of Manchukuo (puppet state) and the upcoming September 18th National Humiliation commemoration, fearing that the Chinese people would express themselves, has been preparing everything for several days before. The areas under the jurisdiction of the Japanese Navy in Shanghai have been divided into two areas, east and west. The so-called east refers to the Hongkou and Yangshupu areas, while the west is near Caojiadu. Each part is assigned a large squadron of armored vehicles to guard everything.

Japanese Warships Anchored in the Huangpu River: The entire fifteenth squadron of torpedo boats has arrived in Shanghai. The four destroyers of the twenty-fourth squadron, "Yanagi," "Momo," "Hinoki," and "Kashiwa," are anchored at the mouth of the Yangtze River. The cruiser "Tenryu," the gunboat "Toba," and the first-class destroyer "Urakaze" are all anchored in the Huangpu River with the flagship "Izumo."

Japanese Consul Notifies Residents: The China United News Agency reported from this city on the 14th that the Japanese consulate issued a notice to Japanese residents, stating that within this week, they should not go to the French Concession and Nanshi lightly to avoid accidental disasters. Due to the Japanese recognition of the puppet state and the upcoming September 18th commemoration day, it is feared that public outrage will be aroused and unexpected changes will occur. Japanese people are asked to be cautious. It is heard that the Public Concession and the French Concession will implement a special curfew order on the 18th.

Jiang and Cai Return to Fujian on the Same Ship 37

Jiang Arrives by Plane from Hankou

Fan Qiwu and Many Others Travel Together

Jiang Guangnai, the Director of Pacification of Fujian Province, after being summoned to Hankou by telegram by Chairman Chiang Kai-shek the day before yesterday, originally intended to delay his return to Fujian until the next sailing date. However, because the next sailing date was too long, he contacted Tang Hai'an, the Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs, who agreed to change the ship's departure time to the afternoon. Therefore, Jiang was able to arrive in Shanghai from Hankou at 4:00 PM and returned to Fujian on the same ship with Cai Tingkai and others at 5:30 PM. The details are recorded separately as follows:

Page 14

Ship's Departure Changed to the Afternoon: When Jiang went to Hankou the day before yesterday, the ship "Zhini Jiana" was scheduled to depart at 10:00 AM yesterday morning. Due to the lack of time, he originally planned to change to the next ship leaving Shanghai. Later, after Tang Hai'an, the Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs, contacted the Zhawa Shipping Company, the company agreed to change the ship's departure time to 5:00 PM in the afternoon. Therefore, after Jiang received a telegram in Hankou, he came to Shanghai at his leisure. However, due to bad weather on the way, the arrival time in Shanghai was delayed. The ship further extended the departure time by half an hour, and Jiang arrived.

Cai and Others Board the Ship in Advance: Tang Hai'an, the Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs, because the ship was changed to depart at 5:00 PM in the afternoon, anticipated that Jiang Guangnai would arrive on time and return to Fujian on the same ship with Cai Tingkai and others. Therefore, he ordered the Jianghai Customs to prepare the "Jinghui" steamboat in advance to wait at the Jianghai Customs pier. As soon as Jiang and others arrived, they could set off. At the same time, for the sake of solemnity, several water patrol officers were specially dispatched by the Jianghai Customs, together with seven detectives sent by the Songhu Garrison Headquarters, to be strictly on guard at the pier. Tang also personally accompanied his secretary to wait at the pier to see them off. However, Jiang and others had not arrived at 4:30 PM. Tang, due to the urgency of time, feared that Jiang and Cai would not be able to leave Shanghai on the same ship. He ordered Green, the port director of the Jianghai Customs, to contact the Zhawa Company to extend the ship's departure time by another half an hour, and at the same time ordered his secretary to notify Cai and ask him to board the ship first to wait. Cai arrived at the Jianghai Customs pier in a car at 4:50 PM and first took the "Jinghui" steamboat with Tang Hai'an and others to the Pudong Landian Chimney Pier to board the "Zhini Jiana" to wait for Jiang to arrive. At the same time, the Jianghai Customs prepared another "Jinghui" steamboat to wait at the pier for Jiang to take. I

Mr. Cai Tingkai at the Pier (Photographed by Xu Dazhang) 38

I

Jiang Rushes to Arrive by Plane: After Jiang Guangnai received the telegram in Hankou, he took the Song's aircraft "Saikesi" to Shanghai at 9:00 AM yesterday morning. Due to poor weather along the way, the aircraft flew very low and slowly. It usually takes four hours to travel from Hankou to Nanjing, but Jiang and others did not arrive in Nanjing until 2:30 PM. By the time they arrived at the Hongqiao Airport in Shanghai, it was already 4:10 PM. Acting President of the Executive Yuan Song Ziwen, Minister of Communications Chen Mingshu, and Song's secretary Huang Chundao all went to the airport to welcome him. Jiang's visit was also to convey Chairman Chiang's opinions on comforting Wang Jingwei and reorganizing the Fujian provincial government to Song Ziwen and others. After Jiang got off the plane, he left the Hongqiao Airport in the same car with Song and Chen. Song and Chen inquired in detail in the car about Chairman Chiang's opinions on the reorganization of Fujian Province. Lu Wenlan, who returned to Shanghai on the same plane as Jiang, was unable to travel with Jiang and Cai due to time constraints, so he returned to his residence to rest.

Jiang and Cai Leave Shanghai on the Same Ship: Jiang left the airport in the same car with Song and Chen at 4:15 PM and arrived at the Jianghai Customs pier at 5:10 PM. He then transferred to the prepared "Jinghui" steamboat to cross the river. Song Ziwen, Chen Mingshu, and Secretary Huang Chundao sent him to the Jianghai Customs pier, bid farewell to Jiang, and returned. Jiang arrived at the Pudong Landian Chimney Pier at 5:25 PM and left Shanghai on the "Zhini Jiana" with Cai Tingkai and others to return to Fujian.

Jiang Guangnai's Remarks: After General Jiang Guangnai boarded the Jingguang ship, he entered the cabin to rest. A reporter from the Central News Agency also entered the cabin and asked Jiang about the results of his visit to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek. According to Jiang, his meeting with the chairman was entirely to report and discuss military affairs and pacification matters in Fujian Province. The reorganization of the Fujian Provincial Government was not discussed. As for the military expenses of the 19th Route Army being supplied by the central government, Mr. Cai had already discussed this with Chiang during his previous meeting. The plan for suppressing bandits is a military secret and cannot be disclosed. When I departed from Hankou this morning (i.e., yesterday morning), the weather was bad, and I was running around by air and land, so I felt very tired. After speaking, the reporter left the cabin.

Fan Qiwu and Others Travel Together: According to those close to Jiang and Cai, the reorganization of Fujian Province has been largely discussed and a considerable result has been reached. Mr. Fan Qiwu has agreed to serve as the financial commissioner and will travel with Jiang and Cai. Otherwise, Fan would not have gone. However, all parties still believe that implementing the reorganization is more difficult. It is heard that in addition to Fan, those who followed included Zhuang Weigang, the Superintendent of the Xiamen Customs, Xu Minghong, the Secretary of the 19th Army, Tang Dehuang, Qiu Zhaochen, and Ye Shaoquan, and many others.

President Wang Refuses to See Guests 39

Wu Tiecheng and Zhang Qun Have Not Yet Met

The Central News Agency reported that Premier of the Executive Yuan Wang Jingwei's illness has been severe for days, with a high fever, so he has refused to see guests. Yesterday morning, Secretary-General of the Executive Yuan Chu Minyi and Minister of Industry Chen Gongbo visited Wang at Pushi Road one after another, but neither was able to meet him. Mayor Wu and Chiang Kai-shek's representative Zhang Qun, who were specially sent by the central government to urge Wang to return to Nanjing early, notified Wang's residence the day before yesterday to convey the central government's and Chiang Kai-shek's intentions, but yesterday, according to Wu and Zhang, they had not yet received a reply from Wang's residence, so they had not yet met with President Wang.
