Ordnance Factory and Artillery Factory Cease Operations 42

The Ordnance Department Sends Personnel to Verify Materials

Merger Committee Holds Third Meeting Today

After the Shanghai Ordnance Factory was ordered to merge with the Jinling Factory, it began to wind up operations. The Ordnance Department specially sent committee members Li Shiqiong and others to Shanghai the day before yesterday to separately verify the materials of the factory in order to relocate them. The artillery factory of the factory was also ordered to stop work the day before yesterday. Factory Director Song Shizhen is scheduled to return to Shanghai today to handle the winding-up. The details are listed separately as follows:

Artillery Factory Ordered to Stop Work: The Shanghai Ordnance Factory has been shut down for six months, but part of the artillery factory was previously extended for six months by the Ordnance Department because it still needed to repair various military supplies sent by the various armies. The required funds were also directly claimed from the department by the factory. The six-month period for this month has expired, so the department ordered the factory to stop work and wind up operations. After receiving the order, the director of the factory, Chen Shihong, in addition to ordering the cessation of work, also went to Beijing yesterday to ask the Ordnance Department for instructions on how to properly resettle the workers after the cessation of work and will return to Shanghai in one or two days.

Committee Members Come to Shanghai to Verify: The Ordnance Department sent committee members Li Shiqiong, Zhou Dianli, and Yang Zijia to Shanghai the day before yesterday to be responsible for handling the remaining materials of the factory and whether they should be transported to Beijing and the disposal methods of scrap copper and iron. After Li and others arrived in Shanghai, they stayed at the Zhenhua Hotel and set up a temporary office in the factory to verify various materials every day. If they are in good condition, they will be transported to Beijing; those that cannot be used will be auctioned off. A small part has now been verified and will be completed soon and returned to Beijing to report back.

Song Returns to Shanghai Today: The factory director, Song Shizhen, previously resigned but was not approved and was ordered by the department to be responsible to the end. Therefore, after Song returned to Shanghai from Qingdao, he still went to the factory to work every day. However, because his wife and others were still in Qingdao to escape the summer heat, Song went to Qingdao again a few days ago to welcome his wife and others back to Shanghai and is scheduled to arrive today to be responsible for the winding-up.

Lin Tongyu Went to Hangzhou Yesterday: Most of the machines of the factory were moved to Hangzhou after the January 28th Incident. The disposal of these machines has also been determined. Yesterday, Lin Tongyu, the chief of the audit section, went to Hangzhou to inspect them as a standard for future relocation.

Meeting to Be Held Today: The merger committee formed by the factory, the Jinling Factory, and the Ordnance Department has held two meetings in Beijing. The location issue has been decided, and a third meeting is scheduled to be held today. Jin Shouyu, the director of the Engineering Office of the committee, also went to Beijing yesterday to participate. Whether to build a factory building will be decided at today's meeting.

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Cables 43

To Revise the Responsible Transportation Regulations

To Express the Hardships on Behalf of Merchants

Hoping That the Government Will Accept Public Opinion

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce cabled the Ministry of Railways, Nanjing:

The Ministry of Railways: Regarding the issue of responsible transportation by the railways, the association previously cabled the Ministry, based on the opinions of the transportation industry, regarding the various obstacles in the regulations, requesting permission to invite the business community to openly discuss them. The request was not approved. Subsequently, the Business Department transferred 300 copies of these regulations to the association, which were distributed to various industries for detailed study. At the same time, the Ministry separately explained them, but the doubts of various industries were not dispelled. They all said that the regulations were contrary to the purpose of convenience and savings. The facts are all there, and they cannot be refuted by empty words. The grain and bean industries are particularly contentious. Recently, they have been actively preparing to switch to water transport in the hope of reducing their burden, which shows that the Ministry's view that the transportation industry alone holds dissenting opinions on the responsible transportation case is inaccurate. The association has a responsibility to express the hardships of merchants on their behalf and also has the ambition to maintain the development of road transport. We deeply hope that the Ministry can accommodate public opinion so that this case can be resolved fairly, so that the national economy and people's livelihood can benefit. Therefore, the various articles that the business community requires to be revised are recorded on a separate sheet and presented by cable. We request that the Ministry examine and approve them for implementation as a matter of public convenience. The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce.

Ministry of Railways Encloses Villages 44

Villagers Petitioned the Municipal Government Yesterday

Requesting Ways to Avoid the Enclosure

Datong News Agency reported that the Ministry of Railways is building a joint transport terminal west of Zhongshan Road in Zhabei, to the Zhenru area. It has sent personnel to measure and survey the base and will soon jointly determine the boundaries with the municipal government to enclose the land for use. It is found that the land enclosed this time is over three or four thousand acres, and the villages enclosed are also over thirty. However, the villagers in the area north of Jiaotong Road, including Wujiajing, Zhangjiazha, and Wangjiazha, believe that their villages can be avoided based on the geographical situation. They specially sent representative Hou Xuanqing to the municipal government to petition Mayor Wu, requesting ways to provide relief and allow them to be avoided. Lin Yannan, the director of the general affairs section, met with them on his behalf. The representative explained in detail the suffering of the farmers after the villages were enclosed, requesting the government authorities to understand the suffering of the people and approve ways to avoid the enclosure. Lin replied that the municipal government would try its best to accommodate the opinions of the people within the possible scope and would refer it to the Ministry of Railways for review and approval. The representative was satisfied and left. The copy of the document presented to the municipal government is copied below:

Petition for the villages enclosed by the Ministry of Railways to build a joint transport terminal, requesting relief and requesting the Ministry of Railways to approve the avoidance of the enclosure to alleviate the people's livelihood and stabilize the community.

It is noted that the Ministry of Railways' enclosing of land to build a joint transport terminal for the two railways west of Zhongshan Road in the Zhenru Pengpu area is originally intended to revitalize Shanghai and facilitate the national transport, and the people dare not oppose it. However, judging from the recent measurements and boundary determinations by the Ministry of Railways, more than thirty villages have been enclosed, especially in the area north of Jiaotong Road, including Wangjiajing, Zhangjiazha, Zhuxiang, Zhujiazha, Zhangxiang, Wangjiazha, and other villages, which are beyond expectations. Upon hearing this, the people felt like a bolt from the blue and were extremely frightened, all believing that their livelihoods would be cut off from now on. Unable to do otherwise, they appealed for relief, hoping for understanding. Clothing, food, and housing are the three major elements of human life. The people have lived in this area for generations and have been engaged in farming as a profession. Their livelihoods depend entirely on the maintenance of agricultural production. Now that the farmland has been bought, the means of production have been lost, and the village houses that provide shelter from the cold have been enclosed, making it impossible for the people to live and work in peace and maintain their lives after the disaster. The people mostly belong to poor families and have been engaged in farming all their lives. They are indeed unable to work or do business halfway. Now that they cannot farm and cannot live, it is tantamount to putting the people to death. Once forced to take a different path and take risks, it will have a profound and significant impact on the national economy and people's livelihood. This is the first reason why relief and avoidance of the enclosure should be requested. Although the Ministry of Railways pays for the land bought from the people and provides relocation expenses for the enclosed villages, the price of land nearby will inevitably skyrocket due to convenient transportation, so the land price paid will not be able to buy the same land again, and the relocation expenses provided will not be able to cover the cost of rebuilding. The hard work of farmers over the years is only enough to make a living, and there are no savings to be used for relocation. Moreover, villages have a close relationship with farming. Farmers live here and cultivate and eat here. If there is any remaining land enclosed, it will be difficult to relocate to other places far away, abandoning their careers. Moreover, rural houses have geographical habits and cannot be built anywhere like in cities. Therefore, since they cannot live nearby and cannot relocate far away, how can they imagine the miserable life in the future? This is the second reason why relief and avoidance of the enclosure should be requested. The base enclosed by the Ministry of Railways covers an area of 3,000 to 4,000 acres, while the land enclosed north of Jiaotong Road, from Jiazhazhai, sloping eastward to Zhongshan Road, covers only 100 acres, but more than ten villages are affected, and more than 300 farmers are affected, with production losses of more than one million yuan per year, which has a significant impact on the folk economy. The enclosed villages are all along Jiaotong Road, and the price of land per acre is mostly several thousand yuan, which is several times higher than the price of land south of the road. It is not cost-effective for the Ministry of Railways to buy it. Moreover, Jiaotong Road was originally the main road between Zhabei, Zhenru, and Nanxiang, but now it is also enclosed, and the road line will inevitably be changed in the future, incurring heavy economic and procedural costs. If it is expanded beyond the existing enclosed base south of the road, there will be fewer villages and lower land prices, and it will be close to the existing Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway. It will also not hinder the original Jiaotong Road. It is beneficial in both reason and principle. This is the third reason why relief and avoidance of the enclosure should be requested. The construction of the joint station by the Ministry of Railways is inevitable, but we hope that it can understand the suffering of the people and provide relief. We respectfully submit this document and request your excellency to examine it, provide relief, and quickly forward it to the Ministry of Railways, requesting it to avoid the villages north of Jiaotong Road to alleviate the people's livelihood and stabilize the community. It is truly virtuous and convenient. Respectfully submitted to Mayor Wu of Shanghai.

Annual Meeting of the Chinese Statistical Society 45

Second Day's Record

The Chinese Statistical Society continued its second general meeting yesterday morning at the ninth floor hall of the Eight Immortals Bridge YMCA. Attendees included members Zhu Junyi, Liu Dajun, Sun Zheng, Yang Runyu, Mao Qihe, Sheng Jun, Jin Guobao, Chen Huayin, Li Quanshi, Tang Qixian, Sun Chaohuan, Lu Zongwei, Zeng Zhaocheng, Chen Zhongqi, Liu Tiesun, Chen Susun, and over thirty others. The meeting commenced at 9:00 AM, chaired by Zhu Junyi. They discussed Chinese statistical terms to unify translations. Each term from the first, second, and third meeting resolutions of the Statistical Terminology Discussion Committee was scrutinized. A total of 133 statistical terms were approved, with one retained. The meeting was then adjourned. After the adjournment, a joint banquet was held by the Pacific International Academic Society, the Chinese Economic Society Research Committee, and the Shanghai YMCA. Chen Liting, a representative of the YMCA and the Pacific International Academic Society, delivered a welcome speech, expressing the hope that various academic groups would cooperate and work together. He Dequi, a representative of the Chinese Economic Society Research Committee, also delivered a welcome speech. Next, Li Quanshi, a representative of the Statistical Society, gave a reply. The banquet concluded. In the afternoon at 2:00 PM, the entire group departed from the YMCA and visited the Customs Library on Xinzha Road. The curator, Ruan Shourong, and the administrator, Chen Shuxun, showed the guests around the library which housed over 10,000 books. The collection focused on Chinese issues and economics. The Customs publications were particularly complete. All issues of the "Bank Weekly," a full set of the "North-China Daily News," and the complete "Weekly Review" were among the rare books. On average, five to six people visited the library daily. The library was established last year, and this year's book acquisition budget was 30,000 taels. The Customs Compilation Office was located on the second floor. It housed the statistics department, specializing in statistical work, equipped with complete statistical machinery valued at over US$200,000. The staff consisted of 41 people, working seven hours a day from 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM and from 1:00 PM to 5:00 PM. The salaries ranged from 20 to 60 yuan per month. Most of the female staff had a secondary school education. Creating a report required three steps. The department head was an American, MEGWINE, and the deputy head was HOBSTOCK. After the visit, the group proceeded to the Public Utilities Bureau in Fenglin Bridge. Director Huang Boqiao gave a welcoming speech expressing his apologies, and the group was divided into four groups to tour the various departments. The entire group of over 30 members toured the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau at 3:30 PM in the afternoon. At 5:30 PM, they attended a reception hosted by the municipal government. Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Secretary-General Yu Hongjun, and Public Utilities Bureau Director Huang Boqiao were present. Mayor Wu delivered a speech, saying, "It is a great honor for me to meet with all of you experts today. Since its establishment, the municipal government has not been able to carry out construction to its full potential for the past five years due to various reasons. There are two reasons for this: (1) the concentration of the economy in the concessions, and (2) the impact of the current situation. Because the economy is concentrated in the concessions, the finances are very difficult. At the same time, the Nanshi and Zhabei districts are reluctant to increase the burden on citizens. Therefore, the municipal government can only spend within its means and cannot spend beyond its means. Therefore, the municipal government has made little progress in construction. I hope that all of you present will provide guidance." Next, Liu Dajun, the president of the Statistical Society, gave a reply, saying, "Among all the cities in the country, Shanghai is number one. The labor dispute statistics of the Social Affairs Bureau are valuable. Last year, I was sent by the National Government to Europe for inspection. Germany and Italy were the best. I have served in the Legislative Yuan and the National Government for four years, and I feel that statistics are very important. Today, on behalf of our society, I would like to express my gratitude to the municipal government and various bureaus." Next, Wu Dajun, the director of the Central Bureau of Statistics, gave a speech, saying, "The government fully encourages the study of statistics. There is a need for cooperation between the government and research groups. Research groups must base their work on the registration and administrative statistical materials produced by the government, to be truthful and accurate. The government must also use the most economical and effective methods to obtain statistical reference materials from research groups. Higher-level governments are too hasty in urging lower-level governments to submit statistical materials, forcing them to falsify reports. To break through this difficulty: (1) can the amount of statistical material needed by governments at all levels be reduced to the minimum? (2) the accuracy of statistical reports from governments at all levels must be guaranteed; (3) the statistical materials produced must have practical applications." He also briefly described the four characteristics of the new central statistical system. The Central Political Conference has already passed the principles of the Statistics Law, and the Legislative Yuan will pass it soon. The above difficulties can all be broken through. Last night at 7:00 PM, the society held a reception on the second floor of the China Society to answer questions from various sectors and to host out-of-town members. Dozens of guests from various sectors and representatives from various organizations attended, along with over 30 members. At the dinner, Mr. Liu Dajun distributed his books "The Statistical Undertaking in China," "English Chinese Population Statistics," "A Comparison of Chinese and Japanese Financial Resources," his edited "China Review Weekly," the English "What Will Happen After the War Against Japan," and the Statistical Daily "Special Issue on International Conferences." President Liu Dajun gave a speech, followed by speeches from the guests, all hoping that the society would work hard on statistical undertakings and serve as the general statistical research organization for the entire country. Finally, the Guangyi Photo Studio took a group photo and the meeting adjourned and concluded.

Record of the General Meeting of the Real Estate Association 46

Proposals to be submitted to the Municipal Authorities regarding Water Fees

The Shanghai Real Estate Association held its twentieth general meeting at 4 PM yesterday. Representatives from various institutions including the Xingye Bank, the Continental Bank, the Donglai Bank, the Central Trust Company, Liu Jingdetang, Zhou Gengji Jingji Company, Huada Foreign Company, Jin Xing Company, Longzhang Company Jingji Company, Yongqing Company, Jiuxing Company, Changtai Company, and others, including Kui Yanfang, Shen Jixuan, Ye Shantao, Wang Zihou, Yu Shian, Yuan Yiqing, Dou Yaoting, Chen Zhongci, Li Bohan, Jiang Bingsheng, and over eighty others were present. Kui Yanfang was elected chairman and Tao Leqin was the recorder. First, the chairman reported on correspondence with the Public Works Department. Next, Li Bohan reported on the issue of increased water prices. The association had organized a special committee to discuss the matter, which decided to adopt both proactive and passive measures to deal with it. The association was preparing to create a "Memorandum on the Drastic Increase in Water Fees," which would list examples of the current water fees calculated using the old percentage (75%) of rent method and the new meter reading method, as well as the increase in multiples, in order to be simple and clear. It would be sent to the Public Works Department and the Board of Directors of the Shanghai Municipal Council and the Public Utilities Committee, requesting them to find ways to provide relief. The following resolutions were passed: (1) The memorandum was revised and approved. (2) A resolution to send letters to all members urging them to dig wells as a passive measure was passed. (3) To make suggestions to the municipal authorities and the public regarding construction: (A) Maintain the calculation of water fees based on rent as the standard (because the additional cost has been added to the water company's expenses). (B) If water fees must be calculated using meters, then (a) the burden on poor people must not be increased; (b) the water company should install water meters in every household, estimate the cost of water supply through testing, and then calculate water fees using meters uniformly, setting three or two levels of water prices according to the level of rent. However, the water fees should be paid directly by the users. The resolution was passed. (4) A resolution to discuss using vernacular Chinese to print a declaration to be sent to all landlords, stamped with the accounting office's seal, and posted in various alleys was passed. The meeting adjourned at around 7 PM.

Local News Two

Investigation of Inferior Goods 48

Hu Futin Assaulted

Turmoil in the Handkerchief Industry

Wang Ruizhang Sued

Wang Ruizhang, the owner of the Xintongfeng Factory in Donggonghe Lane, Simalu (Fourth Road), has been in conflict with Hu Futin, an investigator from the Shanghai Handkerchief Industry Association. Both parties have filed lawsuits in the First District Court. The following is a record of the cause: According to a complaint from a member of the handkerchief industry, after the economic severance with Japan began, on June 7, factories such as Jianxin, Jingxin, and San Yi convened a meeting of the industry. It was resolved unanimously not to buy or sell inferior goods, and violators would be severely punished. All members signed in agreement. More than ten days later, it was discovered that the member Xintongfeng Factory was privately importing inferior goods. An emergency meeting of all members was convened to discuss how to handle the situation. Wang Ruizhang attended the meeting and stated that it was an accidental import and that such behavior would not happen again. However, according to a member's report on August 22, the factory was still importing inferior goods. To be cautious, Hongfu Factory's Hu Futin was specially assigned to investigate the truth. Unexpectedly, Wang Ruizhang not only refused the investigation but even dared to assault and humiliate him, causing Hu to suffer serious injuries, and declared, "My business is my own affair. Who dares to make things difficult for me?" Hu reported the injury to the association, which convened a meeting and decided to expel the factory from membership. Wang Ruizhang also hired a lawyer to publish a statement in the newspaper, stating that the inferior goods stored by the industry before July numbered more than 10,000. His factory only had a small number and had already registered them on file. He had never imported inferior goods since then. He also stated that Hu Futin approached him on August 19 to sell 130 dozen towel handkerchiefs from Hongfu Factory. He agreed to buy 100 dozen, but not the remaining 30 dozen. On the third day, August 22, Hu went to collect the price of the 30 dozen, and a conflict arose during the conversation. On August 24, Hu and Mr. Miao went to the factory, and the money for the 30 dozen was paid in full. The Handkerchief Industry Association was indignant upon reading this and commissioned lawyer Wu Guochang to represent them in a rebuttal, stating that the report to the association about Wang Ruizhang continuing to import inferior goods was not made by Hu Futin. Hu was injured at the factory because he was commissioned by the association to investigate whether he was continuing to import inferior goods. Now, he is fabricating claims in an attempt to deceive the public. Wang Ruizhang also replied, saying that they were protecting Hu Futin, obliterating the facts, not investigating the cause of the quarrel, seeking revenge, and falsely accusing him out of spite. In addition to publishing the details in flyers, the association has also commissioned lawyer Wu Guochang to file a lawsuit against Wang Ruizhang in the First District Court. The lawsuit is as follows: "For refusing to investigate inferior goods and causing injury through assault, please investigate and severely punish according to the law to appease public opinion and deter evil deeds. The plaintiff has been in the handkerchief business for many years. My industry, hating the brutality of the violent sun (Japan), in order to pursue economic severance to bring about its demise, established an association and resolved to vow not to buy or sell inferior goods, violators will be punished, After each member voluntarily signs, unexpectedly after more than ten days, it was found that the defendant violated the rules and privately imported inferior goods. The association convened all the members to discuss the handling method. At that time, the defendant came to the meeting and pleaded that it was a mistake and asked for forgiveness, and that he would never commit the crime again in the future, otherwise he would be willing to accept the most severe punishment. He also made a letter of intent to show that he had no other intentions. Unexpectedly, the defendant lost his conscience, risked being irresponsible, according to the report of the members on August 22, the defendant still imported inferior goods. In order to be cautious, the association specially assigned the plaintiff to go on the morning of the 24th of this month At about 12 o'clock, go to investigate the truth. Unexpectedly, the defendant not only refused to investigate, but also committed a violent assault, causing serious injuries to the plaintiff's chest, which was diagnosed by Nanyang Hospital and a certificate was issued. The defendant's actions constituted a crime under Article 293 of the Criminal Law, and he filed a lawsuit in accordance with the provisions of Article 337 of the Criminal Procedure Law. After receiving the complaint, the court issued a summons, scheduling a hearing for both parties at 11 AM on the 22nd of this month.

Jardine Matheson Comprador 49

Li Ruiling Kidnapped

Abducted on the Thirteenth Night in Tanggu

Shanghai Residence Receives an Anonymous Telegram

Li Ruiling, the comprador of the Jardine Matheson's Northern Shipping Line vessel "Dingsheng", went to Tianjin on the ship this time. The "Dingsheng" could not enter the Baihe River because of the shallow water when it arrived in Tanggu, so it stopped in Tanggu to load and unload goods. It left Tanggu on the 15th to return to Shanghai. Unexpectedly, Li Ruiling was suddenly kidnapped by bandits in Tanggu on the night of the 13th. It was also heard that two clerks from Jardine Matheson's Tanggu branch were also missing. After Li Ruiling was kidnapped, his wife in Shanghai suddenly received a telegram yesterday morning. It was sent from Tianjin and reported that Li Ruiling had been kidnapped. The end of the telegram was not signed, which was very strange. Li's wife did not believe it at first, but at noon, Jardine Matheson also received an official telegram from Tanggu stating that Li Ruiling had indeed been kidnapped and his whereabouts were unknown. Yesterday, the Shanghai office wired its Tianjin branch, reporting to the military and police authorities to investigate Li's whereabouts and notifying his family. The "Dingsheng" can leave Shanghai today to go south. Li Ruiling has no family property, and his monthly income is only enough to make ends meet. The reason for the kidnapping is unknown.

Korean Ticket Collectors 50

Dispute over Severance Pay

Under the Great Clamor of the Crowd

A Large Number of Detectives Came to Suppress

After Using Force, All Were Detained

Transferred to the Japanese Consulate for Handling

Yesterday at 4:30 PM, thirty-one dismissed Korean ticket collectors from the Public Car Company of the Public Concession on Kang'nuo Road (Connaught Road) had a dispute with the company over the collection of severance pay. When the public car ticket sellers and ticket collectors requested a raise from the company and were unsuccessful, they went on strike. The company temporarily ordered thirty-one Korean ticket collectors to act as ticket sellers. But as the ticket collectors did not agree, the company recognized that these ticket collectors were disobedient, hindering business, and they dismissed the thirty-one Korean ticket collectors. The ticket collectors then requested the company in a joint letter to issue two years' salary as severance pay so that they could return to their home country. It is said that the company agreed to issue 150 yuan per person and agreed to issue it yesterday. Therefore, the ticket collectors gathered at the company yesterday afternoon at 4 o'clock to receive it. As there was no result, they turned to the company manager to negotiate, also without result. The crowd then made a great clamor. The company was afraid of causing trouble, so it quickly reported to the Gordon Road police station. A large number of detectives were sent to the scene to suppress them. Unexpectedly, the ticket collectors prevented the detectives from entering and used force. The detectives then arrested all the ticket collectors and transferred them to the police station by truck and sent them to the Japanese Consulate for handling.

Dispute over the Accounts of Public Property between Uncle and Nephew 51

Xu Yucheng Accused

Xu Hands Over Two Kinds of Account Books

One is a Complete Copy

Xu Yucheng, a shareholder of Hengtong Qianzhuang (Money Exchange), was accused of embezzlement by his nephews Xu Wenrong, Wenxin, Yan E'sen, Zhong Hongsheng, and others in the First Special District Court due to a dispute over public property accounts. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Wu Zhen opened the court to interrogate. First, the plaintiff and defendant were asked about their age and address, and then the plaintiff Xu Wenrong's complaint was questioned. According to his statement, the defendant was his uncle. After our family divided the property in the 31st year of Guangxu (1905), a copy of the public property was submitted. It was estimated to be worth more than 80,000 yuan and was managed by the defendant. Until now, the defendant has never handed over the account books, so now we have no way of knowing the exact amount of public funds. However, if the account books are investigated, there must be evidence to prove the discrepancies. However, because the defendant is an uncle, we nephews dare not say that he has embezzled. We have recently learned that the defendant has submitted the account books to the court, and I have requested to copy them. I must wait until after verification before I can know the exact amount. During the defendant's management period, although he entrusted his third uncle to manage the account because he was going to Beijing, after the third uncle died, the defendant took over again. If the third uncle had any deficits during his management, the defendant did not declare them when he took over, which shows that the third uncle had no deficits. Next, according to the defendant Xu Yucheng's statement, I managed the public account from the time the family was divided in the 31st year of Guangxu (1905) until the autumn of the 32nd year (1906). Because I had to go to Beijing, I handed it over to my younger brother Shiheng to manage. Shiheng managed it for a total of four years and two months. Because he died of illness, I took over again. However, after Shiheng died, the account was settled, and more than 1,000 yuan was used up. Now I am accused by my two nephews, which is really inexplicable. My income and expenses are all clear, but three account books were taken away by the plaintiff long ago, and the rest are all there. The defendant's lawyers Yang Linzhi and Ye Shaoying immediately stated that the defendant has brought all the receipts and payments for all these years to the case, and the account books have also been submitted to the court. However, there are two types of account books: one is the original account of funeral expenses, and the other is a copy. The copied account is purely transcribed based on various receipts. Please verify. If there is any fraud, I am willing to accept the punishment. He also submitted several packets of account bills. The plaintiff's lawyer E'sen then requested the court to note that the defendant had admitted that the account books submitted by the defendant were copies. He then recounted the situation where he requested the defendant to hand over the accounts in the civil court. The two defendant's lawyers also presented the accountant's audit report along with their pleadings. After Judge Wu examined and verified them, he found that further investigation was needed and ordered the hearing to be adjourned to another date.

Participating in Chicago 52

Experience of Collecting Exhibits in Hangzhou for the Exposition

Cai Wuji, director of the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau, noted that Dr. Arber, an American, had emphasized the art and handicrafts of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces in his speech in Shanghai last time. He went to Hangzhou with Xu Baohua last Wednesday to discuss the issue of products from Zhejiang province. They repeatedly negotiated with Hangzhou Mayor Zhao Zhiyou, Chamber of Commerce President Wang Zhuzhai, and relevant personnel in the Zhejiang Construction Department. Mayor Zhao convened representatives from various industries in Hangzhou twice and held meetings in the auditorium of the municipal government. Cai Wuji and Xu Baohua successively reported on the participation process and the situation of collecting exhibits. Finally, it was decided to organize a committee in Hangzhou to collect exhibits on behalf of the Shanghai organizers. Wu Gang, the head of the Social Affairs Section of the Hangzhou Municipal Government, was responsible for convening the committee. In both meetings, the Chamber of Commerce and representatives from various industries were able to openly and honestly raise difficult questions for discussion, and Cai and Xu explained them one by one. As a result, it was extremely successful. As for the products from other counties in Zhejiang province, coordination with the Construction Department had been completed. The agricultural products will be handled by Section Chief Zhang of the Construction Department, the industrial products will be handled by Section Chief Wu, and the construction projects will be handled separately by Section Chief Zhu of the Zhejiang Highway Bureau, Director Chen of the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway Bureau, and Director Du. All types of products from Hangzhou and Zhejiang province are allowed to be sent to Shanghai by the end of this year. Cai Wuji and Xu Baohua, seeing that their official business was completed, left Hangzhou by special train last night and returned to Shanghai.

Financial Sector Closed Today for the Mid-Autumn Festival 53

Only the Central Bank Will Be Open

Today (the 15th) is the Mid-Autumn Festival, also known as the Autumn Festival in the Lunar Calendar. As usual, various industries in the city will be closed for one day. The qianzhuang (money exchanges) industry association has published a notice in the newspaper informing all members that they will be closed for one day, and all payments will be made as usual the next day.

Refusal to Drug Use Society replies to the Ministry of Railways by Telegram 54

The Chinese National Anti-Drug Society recently received a telegram from the Ministry of Railways with many misunderstandings and replied to the Ministry by letter yesterday. The original letter is as follows:

"To whom it may concern: We have received your Ministry's telegram stating that it is responsible for transportation and has no relationship with the Jiangsu Province Opium Public Sales. This measure is to relieve the pain of transportation for merchants and promote the prosperity of the railway industry. Our Society expresses its sympathy and trusts it very much. As for the questions asked by our Society, we will reply to them separately as follows: (1) In recent years, railway police have cracked many cases of transporting soil by train, and your Ministry's announcement of the regulations for responsible transportation coincided with the Jiangsu Province's implementation of opium public sales on the same day, September 1, which is easy to cause misunderstandings (2) Many cases of private transportation of opium in Jiangsu Province are transported by railway. Our Society has reports available for consultation at any time (3) Our Society's request to the Control Yuan to thoroughly investigate the truth is different from directly requesting punishment. Even from the perspective of the two phrases 'where there's smoke, there's fire, it's not without reason,' it is also suspected based on previous cases of railway transportation of soil. In short, our Society thoroughly opposes public sales and has no ill will towards your Ministry (4) Our Executive Director Mr. Han's reply to the reporter of the Dalu Newspaper, the phrase 'I don't know how the truth is' does not have the meaning of determining whether it is true or not, and cannot be hastily regarded as our Society admitting that this news is true or not (5) The Jiangsu Opium Public Sales has been rumored for a long time, newspapers have reported it, and people have been talking about it. Our Society's request to the Control Yuan to thoroughly investigate and impeach it is largely based on newspapers. It is incomprehensible that only your Ministry has not heard of it (6) According to the telegram, responsible transportation has nothing to do with public sales, but the matter of soil traffickers transporting opium by train may not be completely eliminated. I dare to ask your Ministry to strictly order the inspectors and railway police on each route to carefully verify. If there is any concealment found, please send the person and the stolen goods to the court for punishment in accordance with the law in order to maintain the opium ban (7) Our Society's purpose is pure, does not ask about politics, does not participate in party disputes, and strives for the struggle against drugs entirely from the position of the people. Our Society's fair attitude has been the same for eight years. The telegram said to satisfy the selfishness of one or two people. I don't know what it refers to. Our Society has enemies and grudges in the fight against public sales, but the action of resisting public sales is really to please the hearts of the people and to disregard the wishes of one or two people. The above answers are all from the bottom of our Society's heart, and I dare to believe that it will be sympathized with by your Ministry. In response, I hope you will take note of it, and I will be very grateful."

US Consul Huston Passes Away 55

The Great American Evening News reports that the US Consul General of this port, Consul Huston, has made outstanding achievements since being transferred to Shanghai in 1928. He recently suffered from illness and did not recover for a long time. He passed away in the Shanghai Sanitarium this morning (14th) at the age of only 44. Those who heard about it regretted it. Mr. Huston came to China in 1915 and served in Nanjing, Hankou, Guangzhou, Tianjin, and other places, and was promoted from vice consul to consul general.

Seaport Quarantine Office Cholera Weekly Report 57

Sixteenth Issue

Wu Lien-teh, Director of the Seaport Quarantine Office and concurrently Director of the Shanghai Provisional Cholera Prevention Office, issued the sixteenth cholera report yesterday (the 14th) as follows: (1) During the past weekend (September 10th), only 110 cases of cholera were discovered in the city (with 10 deaths). This is a decrease from the 131 cases (with 11 deaths) of the previous week. This indicates that the cholera epidemic in Shanghai is showing a clear trend towards becoming milder. The regions and number of cases discovered last week are listed as follows:

Region　Number of Cases　　Number of Deaths

Shanghai City　40　　0

International Settlement　28 (including 2 foreigners)　　4

French Concession　41　　5

Unknown　1　　1

Total Last Week 110 (including 2 foreigners)　　10

Total Previously 4103 (including 7 foreigners)　　301 (including 19 foreigners)

Grand Total 4213 (including 73 foreigners)　　311 (same as above)

(2) It was observed that several weeks ago, the cholera outbreak in the French Concession was more rampant than in other areas, due to the presence of over 12,000 Russian residents, many of whom were refugees. Fortunately, the health authorities of the French Concession administered cholera prevention injections to all residents, regardless of age, so the Russian community did not suffer significant epidemic harm. (3) The weather this week was cool with frequent rain. The highest temperature recorded on September 10th was 88.3 degrees Fahrenheit, the lowest on September 4th was 62.2 degrees Fahrenheit, with an average of 74.0 degrees. Humidity ranged from 55 to 97 degrees, with an average of 80.1 degrees. (4) The cholera epidemic situation in other ports also showed a decrease. The details are as follows:

Number of Cases　　　Number of Deaths

Nanjing (Weekend report of September 10th)　48　7

Hankou (Weekend report of September 3rd)　56　6

Xiamen　Same as above　52　13

Guangzhou　Same as above　3　　0

Tianjin　Same as above　　0　0

(5) Considering that the cholera epidemic situation in the seaports of Tianjin Tanggu, Yantai, Hong Kong, and Guangzhou has become very mild, the Quarantine Office has decided to announce the removal of the designation of these ports as epidemic ports, starting from September 16th. Therefore, ships arriving in Shanghai from Tianjin Tanggu, Yantai, and Guangzhou will no longer need to display quarantine flags upon arrival and can be exempted from quarantine. However, this does not apply to cases where infectious diseases or deaths are discovered on board. As for ships coming directly from Hong Kong to Shanghai, they will still be subject to routine quarantine. Ships coming from Hong Kong via Shantou and Xiamen to Shanghai will still be subject to passenger list quarantine procedures. (6) Regarding the two cities closest to Shanghai with the most convenient transportation, such as Hangzhou and Ningbo, no epidemic reports from those areas had been received. Fortunately, a report was received from Dr. Ding Licheng of the Ningbo Hua Mei Hospital, stating that the first case of cholera in the city was a female discovered on July 9th. Since then, the epidemic has gradually spread, reaching over 4,000 cases, with over 500 deaths. During the outbreak, eight temporary epidemic hospitals were dedicated to prevention and control, but not all patients were hospitalized. The Ningbo Red Cross Hospital and Jiangdong Hospital treated 2,127 cholera patients, of whom 156 died. Ningbo has no running water supply, and residents can only drink well and river water. (7) On September 5th, a sailboat arrived in Shanghai from Huzhou with five crew members. Two of them had cholera. The boat owner, surnamed Song, 52 years old, contracted cholera at 4:00 AM on September 5th and died at 3:00 PM the same day, a total of only 11 hours from illness to death. His youngest son, 16 years old, also fell ill on the same day and died the next morning. The other three were fortunate enough to be unharmed. Upon arrival in Shanghai, they were given cholera prevention injections by this office. This is specially recorded for your attention. (8) Recent investigations show that the beds in the epidemic hospitals are mostly empty. For example, the Xizang Road epidemic hospital, which usually accommodates 60 to 70 patients, now averages only 5 to 6 patients. It is expected that the hospital can be closed by the end of the month. Other epidemic hospitals, such as the Hongkou epidemic hospital on Tangshan Road and the epidemic hospitals attached to the Chinese Red Cross Society, will be closed on September 15th. Only the Isolation Hospital of the Shanghai Municipal Council will continue to operate.

Xiang Sheng Tannery 58

Workers Stage a Full Strike Yesterday Morning

Objecting to the Factory's Dismissal of a Large Number of Workers

Resumed Work in the Afternoon After Persuasion from the Municipal Party Headquarters

The New Voice Agency reports that the Xiang Sheng Tannery on Pingliang Road, Eastern Shanghai, has been in operation for over 20 years and its business has been thriving. However, it suddenly announced the dismissal of a large number of workers in the newspaper the day before yesterday, without prior notice. Upon hearing this news, all the workers were extremely indignant and went on strike yesterday morning. The union reported the matter to the Party and government authorities, requesting mediation. The details are recorded below:

Document Presented to the Party and Government Authorities: The Tannery Workers' Union presented a document to the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Social Affairs Bureau yesterday, stating, "Regarding the Xiang Sheng Tannery's unwarranted dismissal of a large number of workers, we request that personnel be dispatched to legally prevent this in order to maintain people's livelihood. It has come to our attention that the workers of the Xiang Sheng factory reported to the union that they have been working in the factory and have always been law-abiding. The workers could no longer bear the factory's oppression and had to legally join the union to seek job security. Because all the workers joined the union, the factory could not implement its oppressive measures and became even more intensified, suddenly dismissing as many as 18 workers and publishing in various newspapers that the factory used to make white leather but now makes red leather and recruits new workers, etc., in order to deceive the outside world. However, it is not known that the manufacturing of red leather requires the work of gray leather room (originally green leather) workers to peel and manufacture. The factory published in various newspapers that it would switch to making red leather, and the gray leather room workers would have no work to do. This is truly a cover-up, deceiving the outside world and not understanding the language of the leather industry. Now, the factory workers are oppressed by the bourgeoisie, using the poisonous language of deceiving the outside world as a reason to suddenly dismiss as many as 18 workers. The entire factory's workers are extremely indignant and have gone on strike. In addition to the union ordering the workers to strictly maintain order and await a resolution quietly, we hereby request that your (union) bureau promptly dispatch personnel to stop this, so as to facilitate the workers' movement and maintain people's livelihood. We await your orders with utmost urgency and respect."

The Party Headquarters Dispatches Personnel to Mediate: After receiving the union's report, Wang Manyun, Director of the People's Training Section of the Municipal Party Headquarters, dispatched cadre Fan Guoren, along with representatives from the union, to rush to the factory at 11:00 AM yesterday to mediate. However, due to the factory's tough attitude, mediation could not proceed. At the same time, the dismissed workers were advised to return to work as usual, and the striking workers were advised to resume work first and await the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Social Affairs Bureau to mediate according to the law. Thereupon, all the workers accepted the advice and returned to the factory to resume work in the afternoon.

Tonghua Steamer Dispatches Chief Mariner to Rescue 59

Tunan's Rescue Proves Ineffective, Ordered to Sail to Hankou

Jiang Xin Now Dispatched to Find a Way

After the China Merchants Bureau's Jianghua steamer ran aground in Qizhou, the hull was fortunately undamaged. The Tunan steamer, which was dispatched to rescue it, was ordered to go to Hankou to perform duties, leaving it still in danger. Jiangxin Dispatched Again: Li Guojie, General Manager of the China Merchants Bureau, received a wireless report yesterday morning signed by Xu Haisheng, Captain of the Tonghua steamer, and Huang Hongqian, Captain of the Tunan steamer, stating, "Tunan's rescue is ineffective. Please dispatch another capable vessel. The tide is gradually receding. Tunan is ordered to go to Hankou to perform duties." He immediately wired the Hankou branch to have the Jiangxin steamer rush to join the Liji steamer in the rescue after its arrival. It is reported that Jiangxin is not equipped with wireless, and it will have to arrive in Hankou today, wait for passengers and cargo to be unloaded, and then rush to the rescue. The date of departure from Hankou is expected to be the day after tomorrow.

Finding a Way to Get Out of Danger: McKenna, Chief Mariner of the China Merchants Bureau, an Englishman, is experienced in navigation. He was ordered by the General Manager to travel to Beijing on the Jianghua steamer the day before yesterday, then transfer to Qizhou to find a way to tow the Tonghua steamer out of danger. He brought various towing and lightering equipment. It is expected to arrive the day after tomorrow. At that time, the Liji and Jiangxin steamers will work together to tow and rescue it, and a way to get out of danger will definitely be found.

Wusong Baoming Electric Company 60

Merged with Zhabei Water and Electricity Company

Wusong's Electricity Business Can Be Restored Soon

Water Supply Project is Large and Difficult to Implement in the Short Term

Among the electrical companies in this city operated by Chinese businessmen, there were originally six: 1. Zhenru, 2. Baoming, 3. Xianghua, 4. Pudong, 5. Zhabei, and 6. China Merchants. Only the China Merchants and Zhabei companies had generators. Although Baoming also had generators, its power was very weak. As for Zhenru and Xianghua, they used electricity from the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company, and Pudong used electricity from the China Merchants Electric Company. After the war, the Wusong Baoming Electric Company suffered heavy losses, resulting in a declaration of closure. As a result, residents in the Wusong area felt greatly inconvenienced and applied to the city authorities to find a way to restore it quickly. However, the Baoming Company, with huge losses, was unable to continue operations, so it was merged into the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company. The Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities convened shareholders of both companies to discuss the merger. The principle has now been decided. Roughly, Baoming's stocks will be converted into Zhabei's stocks at a discount. Various details are still being carefully discussed. However, Huang Boqiao, Director of the Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities, believes that the electricity in Wusong needs to be restored urgently, so he ordered the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company to start various projects immediately. The company's generator is originally located on Jungong Road, which is very close to Wusong. The construction project is very convenient. It is said that it can be completed soon. As for the Wusong water supply problem, it was originally intended that the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company would install pipes at the same time, but because the project is large, it is difficult to implement in the short term.

Shanghai South Public Bus 61

Bureau of Public Utilities Determined to Restore

Currently Investigating the Reasons for Losses

The Shanghai South Public Bus Company in this city was forced to close down due to excessive losses. Public utilities, according to national laws and regulations, cannot be arbitrarily suspended. A reporter from the Central News Agency visited Xu Yuanfang, secretary of the Bureau of Public Utilities, regarding this matter yesterday. According to him, it is true that the Shanghai South Public Bus Company could not continue to operate due to excessive losses. However, the company is still considering raising funds again to restore operations. If this cannot be realized, the Bureau of Public Utilities will find another way to handle it. In short, the Bureau of Public Utilities will not allow the traffic on the original routes to be suspended for long. As for the restoration method, if the city government has funds, it can be taken over by the city. Otherwise, it can be contracted out to merchants again. Currently, Director Huang is studying the reasons why the company is losing money, so that it can be used as a reference for future city-run or merchant-run operations, so as not to repeat the same mistakes.

Riot Corps Soldiers Died While Pursuing Thieves 64

At 1:00 AM the other night, more than 30 bandits suddenly broke into the home of Tan Ruiqing in Zhaojiadang Township, Fifth District, Shanghai County, intending to rob. They were immediately discovered by the eighth Jia of the nearby Riot Corps, and riot corps soldiers, including Tan Jinxiang, rushed to resist, repelling them on the spot. Tan Jinxiang resumed his courage and pursued them, resulting in being surrounded by the bandits, who fatally wounded him in the head with knives. The township head immediately reported to the district office, and the district chief Xing Zhigang, riot corps assistant Wang Sicheng, and Fifth Public Security Bureau chief Xiao Jianxun led a large number of patrol soldiers and riot corps soldiers to investigate, confirming the facts. District Chief Xing then reported to the local court, and Prosecutor Li was assigned to the township for investigation. He also reported to the Shanghai County Government and the Nanhui County Government, requesting a general order for joint arrest. It is now reported that District Chief Xing, Corps Commander Kong, and others believe that riot corps soldier Tan Jinxiang was loyal and courageous in resisting the bandits and died tragically in the line of duty. They have jointly requested the county government to forward a request to the provincial government for awards and compensation, and intend to organize a memorial service and tribute to console the martyr's soul and inspire encouragement.

Volunteer Corps 65

Platoon Leader, Russian Teenager, Commits Suicide by Gun

Reasons for Suicide Unknown

Burial Arranged by Friends

Olisak Rexki, a 24-year-old Russian platoon leader in the International Volunteer Corps, shot himself in the head with a rifle in the corps barracks on Fujian Road at approximately 7:00 AM the other morning. His brains were blown out and flesh and blood flew everywhere. Upon hearing the sound, a corps member, Russian Meng Xueli Ditai Ke, arrived and found him lying in a pool of blood. He immediately reported to the Central Police Station, which dispatched detectives to investigate. However, the Russian was already dead. The body was transported to the Philand Road morgue. Yesterday morning, the First Special District Local Court was requested to assign Prosecutor Zhan Liangce, along with forensic doctor Zhang Yan and clerk Wang Zuyi, to the morgue to examine the body. According to Meng Xueli Ditai Ke, 35 years old, Russian, the deceased was a friend. No one saw him when he shot himself. There were four people living in the deceased's room, and three of them had gone to breakfast at the time, so the reason for his suicide is unknown. According to the corps commander, Sibili Chu, 35 years old, Russian, residing at 1881 Xiasi Road, the deceased's family is not in Shanghai, and he is now collecting the body on their behalf. Zhan then ruled that the deceased, Russian Olisak Rexki, male, committed suicide with a rifle. The body was handed over to Sibili Chu, the corps commander of the Russian Merchants Corps, to be taken back for burial.

Ruthless Kidnappers 66

Attempt to Extort Money Even After the Hostage Escapes

Wu Tongchao Suffers Unspeakably

One Kidnapper Arrested En Route

Wu Jingyang, a driver from Yimei Electric Company at No. 131, is from Yancheng. He and his wife, Wu Shen, live at No. 3, Fengyu Lane, Hanzhong Road, Zhabei. His father, Wu Tongchao, has some property in his hometown of Yancheng. On March 12 of this year, a large number of bandits in Yancheng suddenly broke into the Wu family armed with weapons and kidnapped Wu Tongchao. At the same time, Tao and Zhou, etc. were also taken away, sending a letter to Wu's family demanding a ransom of $1,500. His son, Wu Jingyang, immediately returned to his hometown and contacted the bandits. Due to ransom issues, an agreement could not be reached. Until April 22, these people committed another crime in Funing County, Jiangbei. The victims reported it, and the authorities dispatched troops to pursue them. As a result, several hostages were rescued on the ship, and Wu Tongchao also escaped at that time, but had already suffered in the bandit's lair for 46 days. Afterwards, the bandits still refused to let Wu go, sending two letters to his son, Wu Jingyang, instructing him to take care of it, otherwise there would be unfavorable consequences. After receiving the letter, Wu ignored it. Until the afternoon of the day before yesterday, Jingyang's wife, Shen, met Wu Hongcheng, a Jiangbei kidnapper in the case, at the intersection of Avenue Edward VII and Rue Cardinal Mercier. She reported it to Chinese Constable No. 2043 and Chinese Detective Zhu Mengwei, who arrested Wu Hongcheng and detained him in the Xinzha Police Station. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the Second Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. According to the police lawyer Wang Yaotang, the incident occurred in Jiangbei and should be transferred to the Jiangbei authorities for trial. However, the victim Wu Tongchao's son, Jingyang, lives in Shanghai, and has recently received two threatening letters from the bandits. Therefore, this case requests an extension for the police to investigate and determine where the incident occurred before deciding whether to accept the case. He is currently asking permission to detain the defendant. Wu Jingyang further stated that since his father was kidnapped, the bandits demanded a ransom of $1,500. I returned to Yancheng to contact the defendant, but a price could not be agreed upon. Later, my father was rescued by the army. He was on a ship hired by the bandits for a total of 40 days and suffered greatly. Afterwards, I received two threatening letters instructing me to take care of it. Because my income is limited, I cannot fulfill the bandits' desires, so I ignored it. The two letters have now been handed over to the police. It was not until yesterday that I met the defendant on the way.

Page 16

I then called the police and arrested him. It turns out that the defendant, Gao Fajin, and the plaintiff, Gao Xijin, are quite influential in the Jiangbei area, with many apprentices under their control. When Wu Hongcheng was interrogated, he confessed that he knew nothing about the kidnapping case. He had just come to Shanghai yesterday and was arrested. After Judge Ge Sixun reviewed the confession, he ordered that Wu Hongcheng be detained and interrogated again next Monday.

French Concession 67

Robbery of a Bill Collector

Suddenly Leapt Out from Zhoushan Road

Thief Li Hanzhang Caught with Guns and Bullets

Ruentai Feng Rice Shop on Doushi Street, Nanshi Chinese Area, has been sending out bill collectors to collect debts from all parties due to the approaching lunar Mid-Autumn Festival. Yesterday, the shop's bill collector, Chen Chunlin, went out to collect debts in the morning. At approximately 5:45 PM, he had collected a total of $1,335 in banknotes, $324 in local bank notes, and two checks, one for $758 and one for $358. At that time, he was about to return to the shop when five bandits suddenly jumped out of Zhoushan Road near Xiaodongmen in the French Concession, displaying handguns and blocking his way, robbing Chen of all the money on his person and fleeing in different directions. Chen then pursued closely behind. One of the thieves turned around and fired two shots, fortunately missing. Nearby detectives also gathered upon hearing the sound and surrounded the area. As a result, thief Li Hanzhang was intercepted and a handgun with live ammunition was seized, and he was taken to the police station. After a thorough interrogation by the police chief, he was ordered to be detained and sent to court for trial.

Municipal Council 70

To Demolish Unauthorized Sheds

The Acting Director of the Works Department of the Municipal Council reported at the last Works Committee meeting that the Board of Directors decided last year that no more sheds would be allowed to be built anywhere, but at the beginning of this year, due to the unsettled situation, strict supervision was not possible. It is now found that there are about 1,000 unauthorized sheds, which should be demolished after giving one month's notice according to last year's case. This matter has also been discussed with the Chinese Council, which believes it is feasible. The Director of the Health Department also stated that the existence of most of these sheds is detrimental to public health, and most of the people living there can find other housing. After research by the committee, it was believed that this matter had been thoroughly investigated last year. For the sake of public health, all unauthorized sheds should be demolished after giving one month's notice according to the old case. This proposal has been approved by the Board of Directors on Wednesday.

Red Cross Request for Exemption from General Tax Denied 71

The Chinese Red Cross Society at Nos. 42, 44, and 26 Jiujiang Road requested exemption from the municipal general tax. After consideration by the Finance Committee of the Municipal Council, it was believed that the address was used as a warehouse and general office, which was not within the Municipal Council's tax exemption standards. Fearing that this would set a bad precedent, it was proposed to reject the request. This proposal has been approved by the Board of Directors.

Cancellation of Tax Exemption for Tuberculosis Sanatorium 72

The General Manager of the Municipal Council reported to the Finance Committee that the Tuberculosis Sanatorium at Nos. 2 to 4 Daxilu was found to be of a commercial nature, and the Health Department also found that the hospital had no charitable work. After consideration by the committee, it was believed that the tax exemption for the hospital should be stopped. This proposal has been approved by the Board of Directors.

Brother Went Mad and Attacked 73

Young Woman, Enraged, Threw Herself into the River to Commit Suicide

At 6:50 PM the night before last, a young woman was seen standing on the Baidu Bridge outside the Suzhou Creek estuary. Taking advantage of a moment when others were not paying attention, she suddenly jumped into the river to kill herself. With a loud splash, waves scattered in all directions. Fortunately, Chinese Constable No. 35 from the Customs Water Police Station was passing by in a boat. Seeing this, he immediately took steps to rescue the woman and brought her to the police station. Under questioning, she stated her name was Yu Jin'e, 22 years old, married to a Mr. Lu. They lived at No. 3184 in the Pu'an Fang neighborhood of Hongkou. "My husband has two elder brothers and one younger brother. The younger brother, named Bingzhang, used to work on foreign ships, but he went mad and lost his job. Now he is at home, beating people arbitrarily every day and is completely unreasonable. Today, I was beaten by him again and have nowhere to seek justice, so I was so angry that I committed suicide," she said. The police officers, considering her to be narrow-minded, offered words of advice and sent a detective to summon her husband's sister-in-law, a Mrs. Qiu, who came to the station to take her home.

A Young Woman Sneaks in Late at Night 74

Pitiful Young Xing Realizes She's Been Lured

Unbearable Memories of Amitabha Lane

At around 12:00 AM the night before last, a young woman, about 17 or 18 years old, dressed in a fashionable qipao, suddenly came to the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway South Station and asked if there was a night train to Hangzhou, which seemed suspicious. The station police saw that she was unaccompanied late at night and looked like she was running away secretly, so they became suspicious and went forward to question her. Her words were evasive, so they took the woman to the police station for interrogation. She stated her name was Xing, a young woman, 18 years old, from Donggong, Jinhua County, Zhejiang Province. Her stepfather was Xing Jingui. "In February of this year, I was seduced and became intimate with He Yihua. We eloped together to Hangzhou and lived at No. 6 Amitabha Lane, Wan'an Bridge. He worked pulling a water cart in West Lake. Later, because life was difficult, my lover He Yihua tricked me into coming to Shanghai to find work. I believed him, so I took a fourth-class train to Shanghai today. But unexpectedly, He had bad intentions and sold me to a brothel to become a prostitute. Therefore, I did not want to and taking advantage of his inattention, I fled to the train station overnight, intending to take a train back to Hangzhou." After the police station investigated and clarified the situation, they prepared a document and sent her to the Women and Children's Relief Association for care.

Liang Zhengpei's Acquittal in Receiving Stolen Goods Case 75

Not Guilty Verdict After Appeal

Previously, the Huaxin Company on Nanjing Road was reported to the General Inspectorate by the Fu'an Company after the Cantonese men Yang Zhongyuan and his nephew Yang Yushan brought 115 dozens of wool sweaters to sell, on the grounds that the goods were stolen by the two Yangs, and Huaxin was suspected of receiving stolen goods. Detective Huang Fusen had already arrested the two Yangs and went to Huaxin to retrieve the original stolen goods, which were handed over to the First Special District Local Court for trial. The final verdict was that Yang Zhongyuan was sentenced to six months in prison, and Yang Yushan was sentenced to four months in prison. Liang Zhengpei, the manager of Huaxin, was fined 400 yuan for the crime of receiving stolen goods. After the verdict, Liang was unwilling to accept it and hired lawyer Zhan Yigang to file an appeal. On the afternoon of the 6th of this month, the Wu, Jiang, and Chuan judges of the First Special Court convened a meeting, summoned the handling detectives and appellants for questioning one by one. After the appellant's lawyer Zhan Yigang and the police lawyer debated with each other, the verdict was announced yesterday. The main text stated, "The original verdict is overturned, Liang Zhengpei is not guilty."

Record of Chen Zhaoqi's Memorial Service 76

Lawyer Chen Zhaoqi of Jiading was young and handsome and cherished compassion. He suddenly passed away in Shanghai in July due to overwork. His fellow villagers Zhu Yinjiang, Gu Jisheng, Zhang Gongquan, Xiang Yuancun, and others initiated a memorial service at the Youth Association on Sichuan Road at 3:00 PM yesterday. In addition to the initiators, more than a hundred people attended, including Jin Jushan, Jin Houcheng, Quan Xuewen, and others. Wu Zonglian was elected as chairman, and he delivered a eulogy. Initiator Zhou Juchen described Chen's brief life. Then, Jin Houcheng, Yang Weiyu, Chen Dazai, and Weng Guoxun gave speeches one after another, generally stating that Chen had been responsible and dedicated throughout his life. This spring, when Jiading was occupied, the fellow villagers in Shanghai organized a relief association, and Chen especially devoted himself to presiding over it, which was deeply admirable. It was a pity that such a promising young man suddenly passed away. It was a loss not only for his fellow villagers but also for society and the country. Finally, Chen Zhaowen, representing the family, gave a speech of thanks, and the meeting adjourned.

Death Caused by Renting a Bicycle Case 77

Liu Xigen Sentenced to Three Years and Six Months in Prison

Zhou Dianchen from Xuzhou rented a bicycle from the Jixing Bicycle Shop at No. 8, near Xinshun Li on Yangshupu Road, at 10:00 AM on August 31. He had a quarrel with the shop apprentice and slapped him in the face. Subsequently, the shop owner, Ji Youdao, together with Liu Xigen from Wuxi and more than ten others, beat Zhou violently, causing him to fall to the ground injured. They then dispersed in a hubbub. Chinese and foreign detectives from the Yangshupu Police Station arrived, took the injured man to the Sacred Heart Hospital by car. He died the next morning due to his serious injuries. Later, the accomplice Liu Xigen was detained and sent to the First Special District Court. After the interrogation, Judge Shen Bing presided over the criminal court yesterday morning and sentenced Liu Xigen to three years and six months in prison. The number of days of detention before the final judgment was commuted, with two days equal to one day of imprisonment.

The Greater Asia Pictorial to be Published on September 18th 78

Shen Shuwei, Zhang Cangsu, and others, the founders of the Greater Asia Pictorial of Liaoning, are preparing to resume publication in Shanghai. The arrangements have been completed. The first issue will connect with the issue that was suspended in Liaoning, making it issue number 324, and it is scheduled to be published on September 18th. It was suspended on September 18th last year and is resuming publication on September 18th this year, which is also an interesting anecdote. The materials collected for the content are very extensive. Regarding photos in the Northeast, such as the Jingbo Lake Waterfall, which is most noteworthy in the Tanaka Memorial, the Sujiang Bridge where Ma Zhanshan resisted the Japanese, and the green gauze tents where the volunteer army camped, are all rare photographs. In addition, the inscriptions by famous people in this city such as Wu Tiecheng, Shi Liangcai, and Zhou Shoujuan add a lot of color. The texts are also masterpieces, and famous novelists Zhang Ziping and He Yiyan have been invited to write. Moreover, the printing is bright, and the paper is clean and white, which is secondary. Each copy is priced at only five cents in foreign currency. It is said that it will be published on the anniversary of the September 18th Incident.

Opening of Pang Xunqin's Painting Exhibition 86

Painter Pang Xunqin returned from France two years ago and set up a painting studio in Shanghai to continue his creative work. Now, in response to repeated urgings from friends, he has selected more than 70 works accumulated over four or five years, including oil paintings, watercolors, and compositions, portraits, and sketches made with pen and brush. From the 15th of this month, they will be exhibited for ten days at the Chinese Art and Craft Society on Avenue Amédeé, French Concession. Pang's paintings received great praise in the Parisian art world when he was in France. After returning to China, whether Chinese or foreigners, anyone who has come into contact with Pang's works has been struck by his unique style and surrealist interest and regards him as a representative of the new trend in Chinese modern painting. It is expected that after the opening, there will be a grand scene in front of the new building of the Chinese Art and Craft Society, with a constant stream of traffic.

The resolution was to forward the matter to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau and the Municipal Party Department. (4) The notice to all labor unions to nominate two representatives to attend and participate in the September 18th Commemoration Meeting was resolved and passed. (5) The motion to oppose Japan's recognition of the puppet organization was resolved with (A) a telegram to the League of Nations, (B) a telegram to the central government requesting troops to suppress the puppet state. (6) The motion to send a telegram to encourage the anti-bandit generals and soldiers was resolved and passed.
